<div><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Hungary" title="History of the Jews in Hungary">Hungarian Jews</a> being selected by Germans to be sent to the <a href="/wiki/Gas_chamber#Nazi_Germany" title="Gas chamber">gas chambers</a> at <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz concentration camp</a>, May/June 1944 (<a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_Album" title="Auschwitz Album">Auschwitz Album</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></div>

<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:transparent;font-size:110%;text-align:center;">Remembrance</div>
<div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;border-top:1px solid #aaa;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;">

<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:The_Holocaust_sidebar" title="Template:The Holocaust sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:The_Holocaust_sidebar" title="Template talk:The Holocaust sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:The_Holocaust_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>

<p>The <b>Holocaust</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[b]</a></sup> also referred to as the <b>Shoah</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[c]</a></sup> was a <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> in which <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and its <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War&#160;II</a> collaborators killed some six million European <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>. The victims included <a href="/wiki/Children_in_the_Holocaust" title="Children in the Holocaust">1.5&#160;million children</a>, and constituted about two-thirds of the nine million Jews in <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continental Europe</a>. A broader definition of the Holocaust includes non-Jewish victims such as the <a href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Romani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation" title="Nazi crimes against the Polish nation">ethnic Poles</a>, members of other <a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Slavic ethnic groups</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aktion_T4" title="Aktion T4">Aktion T4</a> patients who were mentally and physically disabled. An even broader definition includes <a href="/wiki/Hunger_Plan" title="Hunger Plan">Soviet citizens</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">prisoners of war</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_homosexuals_in_Nazi_Germany_and_the_Holocaust" title="Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany and the Holocaust">homosexuals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Persecution of Jehovah's Witnesses in Nazi Germany">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_black_people_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Persecution of black people in Nazi Germany">black people</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_resistance_to_Nazism" title="German resistance to Nazism">political opponents of the Nazis</a>, and members of other smaller groups.</p>
<p>From 1941 to 1945, Germany and its collaborators systematically murdered Jews in a genocide, which was part of a larger event that included the persecution of other peoples in Europe. Under the coordination of the <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a>, with directions from the highest leadership of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>, every arm of Germany's bureaucracy was involved in both the logistics and the carrying out of the mass murder. Killings were committed throughout <a href="/wiki/German-occupied_Europe" title="German-occupied Europe">German-occupied Europe</a>, as well as within Nazi Germany itself, and across all territories controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>. Some 42,500 detention facilities were utilized in the concentration of victims for the purpose of committing gross violations of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>. Over 200,000 people are estimated to have been <a href="/wiki/Collaboration_with_the_Axis_Powers_during_World_War_II" title="Collaboration with the Axis Powers during World War II">Holocaust perpetrators</a>.</p>
<p>Germany implemented the persecution in stages, culminating in the policy of extermination termed the "<a href="/wiki/Final_Solution" title="Final Solution">Final Solution</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Question" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish Question">Jewish Question</a>". Following <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler%27s_rise_to_power" title="Adolf Hitler's rise to power">Hitler's rise to power</a> in 1933, the German government passed laws to exclude Jews from civil society, most prominently the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws of 1935</a> depriving them of citizenship rights. Starting in 1933 Germany built a network of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">concentration camps</a> in Germany for political opponents and people deemed 'undesirable'. After the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">invasion of Poland</a> in 1939 the regime began setting up <a href="/wiki/Nazi_ghettos" title="Nazi ghettos">Nazi ghettos</a> in order to segregate Jews from the rest of the conquered population, and to remove them from the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Germanic_Reich" title="Greater Germanic Reich">Greater Germanic Reich</a>. In 1941, as German forces <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">captured huge territories in the East</a>, all anti-Jewish measures radicalized. Specialized paramilitary units called <i><a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a></i> murdered around two million Jews in mass shootings in less than a year. By mid-1942, most Holocaust victims – men, women and children – were deported from the ghettos in sealed <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_trains" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust trains">Holocaust trains</a> to <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a> fitted with <a href="/wiki/Gas_chamber#Nazi_Germany" title="Gas chamber">stationary gas chambers</a>. Many thousands did not survive the journey. This continued until the <a href="/wiki/End_of_World_War_II_in_Europe" title="End of World War II in Europe">end of World War II in Europe</a> in April–May 1945.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jewish_resistance_in_German-occupied_Europe" title="Jewish resistance in German-occupied Europe">Jewish resistance to the Nazis</a>, although severely limited in terms of resources, was offered in over 100 locations. The most notable was the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Ghetto uprising">Warsaw Ghetto uprising</a> of 1943, when thousands of Jewish fighters held the <a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS" title="Waffen-SS">Waffen-SS</a> at bay for four weeks. An estimated 20,000–30,000 <a href="/wiki/Jewish_partisans" title="Jewish partisans">Jewish partisans</a> actively fought against the Germans and their collaborators in Eastern Europe. <a href="/wiki/French_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="French Jews">French Jews</a> took part in the <a href="/wiki/French_Resistance" title="French Resistance">French Resistance</a>, which conducted a guerilla campaign against both the Germans and the <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy French authorities</a>. Jewish revolts occurred in at least 19 slave labor camps.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_definition">Etymology and definition</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Holocaust" title="Names of the Holocaust">Names of the Holocaust</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_alternate_names">Etymology and alternate names</span></h3>
<p>The term <i>holocaust</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> word <i><a href="/wiki/Holocaust_(sacrifice)" title="Holocaust (sacrifice)">holókaustos</a></i> which refers to an <a href="/wiki/Animal_sacrifice" title="Animal sacrifice">animal sacrifice</a> that is offered to a god in which the whole animal is completely burnt.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[4]</a></sup> Later it came to denote a massacre or slaughter of large numbers of people.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[5]</a></sup> The word <i>shoah</i> (שואה; also transliterated <i>sho'ah</i> and <i>shoa</i>), meaning "calamity" became the standard <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a> term for the Holocaust as early as the 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-YVDefinition_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YVDefinition-9">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Holocaust" was used in the 1950s by historians as a translation of the Jewish word <i>shoah</i> to refer specifically to the German genocide of the Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045-10">[7]</a></sup> The television mini-series <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_(TV_miniseries)" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust (TV miniseries)"><i>Holocaust</i></a> is credited with making the term the usual one for the Jewish genocide in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016201_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016201-11">[8]</a></sup> As the definition of the victims of the Holocaust has expanded to include more than just Jews, <i>shoah</i> continues to retain its meaning as specifically the genocide of the Jews under the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel2010115_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel2010115-12">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[d]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Germans used the phrase "Final Solution to the Jewish Question" to refer to their genocide of the Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006xix_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006xix-15">[11]</a></sup> The term "<a href="/wiki/Final_Solution" title="Final Solution">Final Solution</a>" and similar euphemisms, were used by the Germans as camouflage for mass murder.<sup id="cite_ref-Longerich_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Longerich-16">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span></h3>
<p>The restrictive definition of the Holocaust is that it was a <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> of Jews by the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010412-413_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010412-413-17">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer200210.E2.80.9311_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer200210.E2.80.9311-18">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[e]</a></sup> A broader definition of the Holocaust includes some or all of the non-Jewish victims of the German <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">mass murder</a> campaigns. <i>The Columbia Guide to the Holocaust</i> limits the definition of the Holocaust to Jews, <a href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Romani</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Aktion_T4" title="Aktion T4">Aktion T4</a> patients who were mentally and physically disabled. Its authors write "all three groups, but only these groups, were equal victims of <a href="/wiki/Nazism_and_race" title="Nazism and race">Nazi racism</a> and genocide."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045.2C_51.E2.80.9352_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045.2C_51.E2.80.9352-26">[21]</a></sup> They also offer three additional definitions which include the viewpoints of historians who identify several additional victim groups. One is that the Holocaust only applied to Jews, a second is that there were several different Holocausts, each affecting a separate group, and a third would include all German racially-motivated crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200051.E2.80.9352_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200051.E2.80.9352-27">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Timothy_D._Snyder" title="Timothy D. Snyder">Timothy Snyder</a> wrote: "The term Holocaust is sometimes used in two other ways: to mean all German killing policies during the war, or to mean all oppression of Jews by the Nazi regime".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010412_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010412-28">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Broader definitions of so-called "parallel Holocausts" include the Soviet POWs who died as a result of mistreatment due to German racial policies,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200048.E2.80.9349_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200048.E2.80.9349-29">[24]</a></sup> the non-Jewish ethnic Poles who died from the conditions that resulted from the German occupation of Poland, the Soviet citizens who died due to similar conditions in occupied parts of the Soviet Union,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200049.E2.80.9350_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200049.E2.80.9350-30">[25]</a></sup> mentally and physically disabled people who were killed in Nazi Germany's eugenics program,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200048_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200048-31">[26]</a></sup> the Gypsies, or the Romani and Sinti,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200047.E2.80.9348_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200047.E2.80.9348-32">[27]</a></sup> homosexuals, Jehovah's Witnesses and other religious dissenters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200050.E2.80.9351_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200050.E2.80.9351-33">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distinctive_features">Distinctive features</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WW2-Holocaust-Europe.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/WW2-Holocaust-Europe.png/330px-WW2-Holocaust-Europe.png" width="330" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/WW2-Holocaust-Europe.png/495px-WW2-Holocaust-Europe.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/WW2-Holocaust-Europe.png/660px-WW2-Holocaust-Europe.png 2x" data-file-width="1310" data-file-height="1090" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WW2-Holocaust-Europe.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Territories of the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a>, olive green. <a href="/wiki/Ghettos_in_German-occupied_Europe_(1939%E2%80%931944)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghettos in German-occupied Europe (1939–1944)">Ghettos</a> were established in which Jews were confined before they were shipped off to <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genocidal_state">Genocidal state</span></h3>
<p>The entirety of German society conducted activities relating to the genocide, turning the <a href="/wiki/Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a> into what one Holocaust scholar, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Berenbaum" title="Michael Berenbaum">Michael Berenbaum</a>, has called "a genocidal state".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006103_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006103-34">[29]</a></sup> Bureaucrats were involved with finding records to identify who was a Jew, the confiscation of property, and the scheduling of trains that deported Jews. Companies fired Jewish employees, and later employed Jews as slave labour. Universities dismissed Jewish students and faculty. German pharmaceutical companies tested drugs on camp prisoners; other companies built the <a href="/wiki/Crematoria" class="mw-redirect" title="Crematoria">crematoria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006103_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006103-34">[29]</a></sup> As prisoners entered the death camps, they were ordered to surrender all personal property, which was catalogued and tagged before it was sent to Germany to be reused or recycled.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad1987154.E2.80.93159_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad1987154.E2.80.93159-35">[30]</a></sup> Through a <a href="/wiki/Max_Heiliger" title="Max Heiliger">concealed account</a>, the German National Bank helped <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">launder valuables</a> stolen from the victims.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel167_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel167-36">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Saul_Friedl%C3%A4nder" title="Saul Friedländer">Saul Friedländer</a> writes that: "Not one social group, not one religious community, not one scholarly institution or professional association in Germany and throughout Europe declared its solidarity with the Jews"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder2007xxi_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder2007xxi-37">[32]</a></sup> He writes that some Christian churches "declared that converted Jews should be regarded as part of the flock, but even then only up to a point".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder2007xxi_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder2007xxi-37">[32]</a></sup> Friedländer argues that this makes the Holocaust distinctive because <a href="/wiki/Antisemitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic">antisemitic</a> policies were able to "unfold to their most extreme levels without the interference of any major countervailing interests".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder2007xxi_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder2007xxi-37">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideology_and_scale">Ideology and scale</span></h3>
<p>Historian <a href="/wiki/Yehuda_Bauer" title="Yehuda Bauer">Yehuda Bauer</a> argues that the Holocaust was based on ideology and myths rather than on practical considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer200248_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer200248-38">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eberhard_J%C3%A4ckel" title="Eberhard Jäckel">Eberhard Jäckel</a> argues that one distinctive feature of the Holocaust was that it was the first time in which a state put the full power behind its declaration that a whole people would be completely wiped out without exception and as quickly as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaier199753_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaier199753-39">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Evans" title="Richard J. Evans">Richard J. Evans</a> noted the "obsessivness" and "desire to be comprehensive" of the Germans during the Holocaust as they tried to eliminate the Jews throughout the world, not just in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2015376.E2.80.93377_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2015376.E2.80.93377-40">[35]</a></sup> Nazi thought held that the Jews were, according to David Bloxham, "a parasitical, polluting people" who were corrosive to all that they interacted with. Other "races" or groups were also considered inferior, but not to the same degree of concern as Jews. These groups included Romanis and blacks, as well as the disabled, criminals, and other social misfits.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009140.E2.80.93141_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009140.E2.80.93141-41">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The killings were systematically conducted in virtually all areas of <a href="/wiki/Occupied_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupied Europe">German-occupied territory</a> in more than 20 occupied countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnited_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum19967_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnited_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum19967-42">[37]</a></sup> Close to 3 million Jews in occupied Poland and between 700,000 and 2.5 million Jews in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> were killed. Hundreds of thousands more Jews also died in the rest of German-occupied Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrowe2008447_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrowe2008447-43">[38]</a></sup> Discussions at the <a href="/wiki/Wannsee_Conference" title="Wannsee Conference">Wannsee Conference</a> make it clear that the German "final solution of the Jewish question" included <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a> and all the neutral states in Europe, such as <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001289_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001289-44">[39]</a></sup> Over 200,000 people are estimated to have been Holocaust perpetrators.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStone2010109_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStone2010109-45">[40]</a></sup> Without the help of local collaborators, the Germans would not have been able to extend the Holocaust completely across most of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009130_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009130-46">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrialized_murder">Industrialized murder</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">Extermination camp</a></div>
<p>The use of extermination camps, or death camps, equipped with gas chambers, for the systematic mass extermination of people was an unprecedented feature of the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2015385_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2015385-47">[42]</a></sup> The German camps of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Reinhard" title="Operation Reinhard">Operation Reinhard</a> were designed and built for the sole purpose of killing Jews as quickly and efficiently as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGellatelyStoltzfus2001216_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGellatelyStoltzfus2001216-48">[43]</a></sup> Stationary facilities to which the victims were <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_train" title="Holocaust train">transported by rail</a> for mass extermination grew out of German experimentation with poison gas during the secret <a href="/wiki/Action_T4" class="mw-redirect" title="Action T4">Action T4</a> euthanasia programme against mental patients.<sup id="cite_ref-Gassing_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gassing-49">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antisemitism_and_racism">Antisemitism and racism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Germany" title="History of the Jews in Germany">History of the Jews in Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">Antisemitism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity_and_antisemitism" title="Christianity and antisemitism">Christianity and antisemitism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_and_antisemitism" title="Martin Luther and antisemitism">Martin Luther and antisemitism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religious_antisemitism" title="Religious antisemitism">Religious antisemitism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racial_antisemitism" title="Racial antisemitism">Racial antisemitism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_boycott_of_Jewish_businesses" title="Nazi boycott of Jewish businesses">Nazi boycott of Jewish businesses</a></div>
<p>Throughout the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> in Europe, Jews were subjected to antisemitism based on Christian theology, which blamed them for rejecting and killing <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>. Even after the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> continued to persecute Jews, accusing them of <a href="/wiki/Blood_libel" title="Blood libel">blood libels</a> and subjecting them to <a href="/wiki/Pogroms" class="mw-redirect" title="Pogroms">pogroms</a> and expulsions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones2006148_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones2006148-50">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen201614.E2.80.9317_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen201614.E2.80.9317-51">[46]</a></sup> The second half of the 19th century saw the emergence in <a href="/wiki/German_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="German empire">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> of the <a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lkisch_movement" title="Völkisch movement"><i>Völkisch</i> movement</a> which was developed by such thinkers as <a href="/wiki/Houston_Stewart_Chamberlain" title="Houston Stewart Chamberlain">Houston Stewart Chamberlain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_de_Lagarde" title="Paul de Lagarde">Paul de Lagarde</a>. The movement presented a pseudo-scientific, biologically based form of <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> that viewed Jews as a <a href="/wiki/Race_(human_categorization)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (human categorization)">race</a> whose members were locked in mortal combat with the <a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Aryan race</a> for world domination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer200247.E2.80.9349_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer200247.E2.80.9349-52">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14469,_Berlin,_Boykott-Posten_vor_j%C3%BCdischem_Warenhaus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14469%2C_Berlin%2C_Boykott-Posten_vor_j%C3%BCdischem_Warenhaus.jpg/260px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14469%2C_Berlin%2C_Boykott-Posten_vor_j%C3%BCdischem_Warenhaus.jpg" width="260" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14469%2C_Berlin%2C_Boykott-Posten_vor_j%C3%BCdischem_Warenhaus.jpg/390px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14469%2C_Berlin%2C_Boykott-Posten_vor_j%C3%BCdischem_Warenhaus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14469%2C_Berlin%2C_Boykott-Posten_vor_j%C3%BCdischem_Warenhaus.jpg/520px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14469%2C_Berlin%2C_Boykott-Posten_vor_j%C3%BCdischem_Warenhaus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="520" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14469,_Berlin,_Boykott-Posten_vor_j%C3%BCdischem_Warenhaus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Antisemitism in Germany: <a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">SA</a> troopers urge a national boycott of Jewish businesses outside <a href="/wiki/Israel%27s_Department_Store" title="Israel's Department Store">Israel's Department Store</a> in Berlin, 1 April 1933. All signs read: "Germans! Defend yourselves! Don't buy from Jews."<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[48]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the German Empire, <i>völkisch</i> notions and <a href="/wiki/Scientific_racism" title="Scientific racism">pseudo-scientific</a> racism had become commonplace and were accepted throughout Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans198969.E2.80.9370_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans198969.E2.80.9370-54">[49]</a></sup> with the professional classes of the country adopting an ideology that did not see humans as racial equals with equal hereditary value.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedlander1994495.E2.80.93496_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedlander1994495.E2.80.93496-55">[50]</a></sup> Though the <i>völkisch</i> parties had some support in elections at first, by 1914 they no longer were influential. This did not mean that antisemitism had disappeared, instead it was incorporated into the platforms of some mainstream political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans198969.E2.80.9370_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans198969.E2.80.9370-54">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany_after_World_War_I">Germany after World War I</span></h3>
<p>The political situation in Germany and elsewhere in Europe after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> (1914–1918) also contributed to the rise of virulent antisemitism. Many Germans did not accept the fact that their country had been defeated in battle, giving rise to the <a href="/wiki/Stab-in-the-back_myth" title="Stab-in-the-back myth">Stab-in-the-back myth</a>. The myth insinuated that it was disloyal politicians, chiefly Jews and Communists, who orchestrated Germany's surrender. Inflaming the anti-Jewish sentiment espoused by the myth was the apparent overrepresentation of ethnic Jews in the leadership of Communist revolutionary governments in Europe, such as <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Toller" title="Ernst Toller">Ernst Toller</a>, who was the head of a short-lived revolutionary government in <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>. This perceived overrepresentation contributed to the canard of <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Bolshevism" title="Jewish Bolshevism">Jewish Bolshevism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The economic strains of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> led some in the German medical establishment to advocate the <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanization</a> of the "incurable" mentally and physically disabled as a cost-saving measure in order to free up money to care for the curable.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2004377.E2.80.93378_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2004377.E2.80.93378-57">[52]</a></sup> By the time the Nazis came to power in 1933, a tendency already existed in the German social policy which advocated the saving of the racially "valuable" while seeking to rid society of the racially "undesirable".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeukert1994289_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeukert1994289-58">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_German_Workers%27_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="National Socialist German Workers' Party">National Socialist German Workers' Party</a>, or Nazi Party, originated in 1920<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder197663_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder197663-59">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[f]</a></sup> as an offshoot of the <i>völkisch</i> movement and it adopted that movement's form of antisemitism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer200247_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer200247-61">[55]</a></sup> Early antisemites in the Nazi Party included <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Rosenberg" title="Alfred Rosenberg">Alfred Rosenberg</a>, who in the 1920s wrote antisemitic articles in the <i><a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lkischer_Beobachter" title="Völkischer Beobachter">Völkischer Beobachter</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Dietrich_Eckart" title="Dietrich Eckart">Dietrich Eckart</a>, publisher of the <i>Völkischer Beobachter</i>. Rosenberg's vision of a secretive Jewish conspiracy ruling the world would influence Hitler's views of Jews by making them the driving force behind communism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil199041.E2.80.9343_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil199041.E2.80.9343-62">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Hitler's_world_view"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hitler.27s_world_view">Hitler's world view</span></h3>
<p>The origin and first expression of Hitler's antisemitism remain a matter of debate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199860_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199860-63">[57]</a></sup> Central to Hitler's philosophy was the idea of expansion and <i><a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">lebensraum</a></i> (living space) for Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen201652_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen201652-64">[58]</a></sup> Hitler was open about his hatred of Jews and he subscribed to most of the common antisemitic stereotypes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen201653.E2.80.9354_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen201653.E2.80.9354-65">[59]</a></sup> From the early 1920s onwards, Hitler linked the Jews with germs and claimed that they should be dealt with in exactly the same way. Hitler viewed <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> as a Jewish doctrine and proclaimed that he was fighting against "<a href="/wiki/Jewish_Bolshevism" title="Jewish Bolshevism">Jewish Marxism</a>". He believed that Jews had created communism as part of a conspiracy to destroy Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen201656_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen201656-66">[60]</a></sup> In the 1920s, the journalist Joseph Hell claimed that in response to being asked what he would do to the Jews once he gained power, Hitler said that his "first and foremost task will be the annihilation of the Jews".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFleming199417_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFleming199417-67">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_Nazi_Germany">Rise of Nazi Germany</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Dictatorship_and_repression_(1933–1939)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dictatorship_and_repression_.281933.E2.80.931939.29">Dictatorship and repression (1933–1939)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Anti-Jewish_legislation_in_prewar_Nazi_Germany" title="Anti-Jewish legislation in prewar Nazi Germany">Anti-Jewish legislation in prewar Nazi Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany" title="Racial policy of Nazi Germany">Racial policy of Nazi Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haavara_Agreement" title="Haavara Agreement">Haavara Agreement</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jews_escaping_from_German-occupied_Europe_to_the_United_Kingdom" title="Jews escaping from German-occupied Europe to the United Kingdom">Jews escaping from German-occupied Europe to the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>With the establishment of the Third Reich, German leaders proclaimed the rebirth of the "people's community" of solidarity against internal and external enemies (<i><a href="/wiki/Volksgemeinschaft" title="Volksgemeinschaft">Volksgemeinschaft</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritzsche200938.E2.80.9339_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritzsche200938.E2.80.9339-68">[62]</a></sup> Nazi German policies divided the population into two categories, the "national comrades" (<i>Volksgenossen</i>) who belonged to the <i>Volksgemeinschaft</i>, and the "community aliens" (<i>Gemeinschaftsfremde</i>) who did not. The enemies were divided into three main groups of people, the "racial" enemies such as the Jews and the Romani people viewed as "blood" enemies; political opponents of Nazism such as Marxists, liberals, Christians and the "reactionaries" viewed as wayward "national comrades"; and moral opponents such as homosexuals, the "work-shy", and habitual criminals, who were also seen as wayward "national comrades". The last two groups were to be sent to concentration camps for "re-education", with the aim of eventual absorption into the <i>Volksgemeinschaft</i>. "Racial" enemies such as the Jews could never belong to the <i>Volksgemeinschaft</i>; they were to be totally removed from society.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENoakesPridham1983499_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENoakesPridham1983499-69">[63]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jewish_refugees_at_Croydon_airport_1939.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Jewish_refugees_at_Croydon_airport_1939.jpg/260px-Jewish_refugees_at_Croydon_airport_1939.jpg" width="260" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Jewish_refugees_at_Croydon_airport_1939.jpg/390px-Jewish_refugees_at_Croydon_airport_1939.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Jewish_refugees_at_Croydon_airport_1939.jpg/520px-Jewish_refugees_at_Croydon_airport_1939.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1306" data-file-height="1031" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jewish_refugees_at_Croydon_airport_1939.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jewish refugees being marched away by British police at <a href="/wiki/Croydon_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Croydon airport">Croydon airport</a> in March 1939. They were put on a flight to Warsaw.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Leading up to the <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_March_1933" title="German federal election, March 1933">March 1933 <i>Reichstag</i> elections</a> and after it, the Nazis intensified their campaign of violence against their opponents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann201528.E2.80.9330_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann201528.E2.80.9330-70">[64]</a></sup> They set up concentration camps for the extrajudicial imprisonment of their opponents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann201532.E2.80.9338_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann201532.E2.80.9338-71">[65]</a></sup> One of the first, at <a href="/wiki/Dachau_concentration_camp" title="Dachau concentration camp">Dachau</a>, opened on 9 March 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert198532_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert198532-72">[66]</a></sup> Initially the camp primarily contained Communists and Social Democrats.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2012155_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2012155-73">[67]</a></sup> Other early prisons were consolidated by mid-1934 into purpose-built camps outside the cities, run exclusively by the SS.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann201584.E2.80.9386_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann201584.E2.80.9386-74">[68]</a></sup> The initial purpose of the camps was to serve as a deterrent by terrorizing those Germans who did not conform to social norms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeukert1987214_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeukert1987214-75">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout the 1930s, the legal, economic, and social rights of Jews were steadily restricted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199733_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199733-76">[70]</a></sup> On 1 April 1933, a <a href="/wiki/Nazi_boycott_of_Jewish_businesses" title="Nazi boycott of Jewish businesses">boycott of Jewish businesses</a> occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2004434.E2.80.93435_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2004434.E2.80.93435-77">[71]</a></sup> On 7 April 1933, the <a href="/wiki/Law_for_the_Restoration_of_the_Professional_Civil_Service" title="Law for the Restoration of the Professional Civil Service">Law for the Restoration of the Professional Civil Service</a> was passed which excluded all Jews and other "non-Aryans" from the civil service.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurleighWippermann199178_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurleighWippermann199178-78">[72]</a></sup> Jewish lawyers were <a href="/wiki/Disbarment" title="Disbarment">disbarred</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199729_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199729-79">[73]</a></sup> Jewish students were restricted by quotas from attending schools and universities,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurleighWippermann199178_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurleighWippermann199178-78">[72]</a></sup> from belonging to the Journalists' Association, and from being owners or editors of newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199733_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199733-76">[70]</a></sup> Jewish businesses were also targeted for either closure or "Aryanisation", the forcible sale to Germans. Of the approximately 50,000 Jewish-owned businesses in Germany in 1933, only about 7,000 were still Jewish-owned in April 1939. Accompanying the removal of the Jews from economic life, they were also gradually restricted from most social activities and public areas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurleighWippermann199186.E2.80.9387_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurleighWippermann199186.E2.80.9387-80">[74]</a></sup> Works by Jewish composers,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder1997134_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder1997134-81">[75]</a></sup> Jewish authors,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005158.E2.80.93159_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005158.E2.80.93159-82">[76]</a></sup> and Jewish artists were excluded from publications, performances, or exhibitions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005169_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005169-83">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuremberg_Laws">Nuremberg Laws</span></h3>
<p>In September 1935, Hitler introduced the three <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005543.E2.80.93544_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005543.E2.80.93544-84">[78]</a></sup> which prohibited Germans and those of "kindred blood"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005550_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005550-85">[79]</a></sup> from having sexual relations with or marrying Jews<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGellately2001122.E2.80.93123_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGellately2001122.E2.80.93123-86">[80]</a></sup> or Romanis.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009149_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009149-87">[81]</a></sup> The laws also stripped German Jews of their citizenship and deprived them of all <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005544-545_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005544-545-88">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[g]</a></sup> At the same time the German government used propaganda to justify the need for a restrictive law,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005539_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005539-91">[84]</a></sup> grouping these "crimes" under the concept of <i><a href="/wiki/Rassenschande" title="Rassenschande">Rassenschande</a></i> (racial shame).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005551_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005551-92">[85]</a></sup> Difficulties arose over the precise definition of who was a Jew and what to do with the offspring and descendants of earlier mixed marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009163.E2.80.93164_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009163.E2.80.93164-93">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emigration">Emigration</span></h3>
<p>Nazi racial policy was aimed at forcing Jews to emigrate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001285_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001285-94">[87]</a></sup> Fifty thousand German Jews left Germany by the end of 1934,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199820_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199820-95">[88]</a></sup> and by the end of 1938, approximately half the German Jewish population had left the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001285_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001285-94">[87]</a></sup> Among the prominent Jews who left was the conductor <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Walter" title="Bruno Walter">Bruno Walter</a>, who fled after being told that the hall of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Philharmonic" title="Berlin Philharmonic">Berlin Philharmonic</a> would be burned down if he conducted a concert there.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder19971_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder19971-96">[89]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>, who was abroad when Hitler came to power, never returned to Germany. He was expelled from the <a href="/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_Society" title="Kaiser Wilhelm Society">Kaiser Wilhelm Society</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Prussian Academy of Sciences">Prussian Academy of Sciences</a>, and his citizenship was revoked.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199712_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199712-97">[90]</a></sup> Other Jewish scientists, including <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Hertz" class="mw-redirect" title="Gustav Hertz">Gustav Hertz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Schr%C3%B6dinger" title="Erwin Schrödinger">Erwin Schrödinger</a>, lost their teaching positions and left the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans200516_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans200516-98">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1938, <a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">Germany annexed Austria</a>, which exposed the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Austria" title="History of the Jews in Austria">Jews of Austria</a> to German antisemitism. Austrian Nazis broke into Jewish shops, stole from Jewish homes and businesses, and forced Jews to perform humiliating acts such as scrubbing the streets or cleaning toilets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016147.E2.80.93150_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016147.E2.80.93150-99">[92]</a></sup> Jewish businesses were "Aryanised" and all of the legal restrictions on Jews in Germany were imposed upon Austrian Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016153.E2.80.93155_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016153.E2.80.93155-100">[93]</a></sup> In August <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann" title="Adolf Eichmann">Adolf Eichmann</a> was put in charge of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Agency_for_Jewish_Emigration_in_Vienna" title="Central Agency for Jewish Emigration in Vienna">Central Agency for Jewish Emigration</a>, which centralised the process of emigration and led about 100,000 Austrian Jews to leave the country by May 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005659.E2.80.93661_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005659.E2.80.93661-101">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kristallnacht_and_afterwards"><i>Kristallnacht</i> and afterwards</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burning_Synagoge_Kristallnacht_1938.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Burning_Synagoge_Kristallnacht_1938.jpg/220px-Burning_Synagoge_Kristallnacht_1938.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Burning_Synagoge_Kristallnacht_1938.jpg/330px-Burning_Synagoge_Kristallnacht_1938.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Burning_Synagoge_Kristallnacht_1938.jpg/440px-Burning_Synagoge_Kristallnacht_1938.jpg 2x" data-file-width="507" data-file-height="347" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burning_Synagoge_Kristallnacht_1938.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The synagogue in <a href="/wiki/Siegen" title="Siegen">Siegen</a> burning, 10 November 1938.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 7 November 1938, <a href="/wiki/Herschel_Grynszpan" title="Herschel Grynszpan">Herschel Grynszpan</a>, a Polish Jew, assassinated the German diplomat <a href="/wiki/Ernst_vom_Rath" title="Ernst vom Rath">Ernst vom Rath</a> in Paris in retaliation for the expulsion of his parents from Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005580_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005580-102">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[h]</a></sup> When vom Rath died on 9 November, the government used his death as a pretext to instigate a <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">pogrom</a> against the Jews in the Third Reich. Although the government claimed the pogrom was spontaneous, it was actually planned and ordered by Hitler and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels" title="Joseph Goebbels">Goebbels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005581.E2.80.93582_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005581.E2.80.93582-105">[97]</a></sup> This event became known as <i><a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></i> ("Crystal Night" or the "Night of Broken Glass")<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder1976201_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder1976201-106">[98]</a></sup> and it was carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">SA</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005583.E2.80.93584_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005583.E2.80.93584-107">[99]</a></sup> although Germans who were not members of either group took part also. In some areas, the violence started before the SS or SA arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009168_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009168-108">[100]</a></sup> Over 7,500 Jewish shops and more than 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogues</a> were either damaged or destroyed. The damage was estimated at 39 million Reichmarks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016184.E2.80.93185_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016184.E2.80.93185-109">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The death toll was officially given as 91, but it may have been higher.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016187_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016187-110">[102]</a></sup> 30,000 men were sent to the Dachau, <a href="/wiki/Buchenwald_concentration_camp" title="Buchenwald concentration camp">Buchenwald</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_concentration_camp" title="Sachsenhausen concentration camp">Sachsenhausen</a> concentration camps,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005591_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005591-111">[103]</a></sup> but many of them were released within weeks. Only 2,000 of them remained in the camps by early 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016200_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016200-112">[104]</a></sup> German Jewry was made collectively responsible for restitution of the damage resulting from the pogrom, and they also had to pay an "atonement tax" of more than a billion Reichsmarks. Insurance payments for damages to their property were confiscated by the government. A decree on 12 November barred Jews from most of the remaining occupations that they had not yet been banned from.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005595.E2.80.93596_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005595.E2.80.93596-113">[105]</a></sup> After <i>Kristallnacht</i>, Jews caught in the Third Reich stepped up their efforts to leave the country. It also marked the end of any sort of public Jewish activity and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBen-RafaelGl.C3.B6cknerSternberg201125.E2.80.9326_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBen-RafaelGl.C3.B6cknerSternberg201125.E2.80.9326-114">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_solution_and_resettlement">Territorial solution and resettlement</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_Plan" title="Madagascar Plan">Madagascar Plan</a></div>
<p>Before <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Germany considered mass deportation of German, and later European, Jewry from Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder1989224-225_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder1989224-225-115">[107]</a></sup> Among the areas considered for possible resettlement were <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">British Palestine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199762.E2.80.9363_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder199762.E2.80.9363-116">[108]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/French_Madagascar" title="French Madagascar">French Madagascar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning2001_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning2001-117">[109]</a></sup> After the war began, German leaders considered the idea of deporting Europe's Jews to <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Palestine was the only location to which any German relocation plan produced any results, via the <a href="/wiki/Haavara_Agreement" title="Haavara Agreement">Haavara Agreement</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Zionist_Federation_of_Germany" title="Zionist Federation of Germany">Zionist Federation of Germany</a> and the German government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel2010264_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel2010264-119">[111]</a></sup> This agreement resulted in the transfer of about 60,000 German Jews and $100<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million from Germany to Palestine, but it ended with the outbreak of World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChase1999xiii_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChase1999xiii-120">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 1940, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> became the focus of German deportation efforts<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning2001_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning2001-117">[109]</a></sup> because it had unfavorable living conditions that would hasten deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENaimark200173_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENaimark200173-121">[113]</a></sup> Some German leaders began discussing the idea in 1938 and <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann" title="Adolf Eichmann">Adolf Eichmann</a>'s office was ordered to carry out resettlement planning, but no evidence of planning exists until after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">fall of France</a> in June 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning200481.E2.80.9385_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning200481.E2.80.9385-122">[114]</a></sup> But the inability to defeat Great Britain prevented the movement of Jews across the seas,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning200488_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning200488-123">[115]</a></sup> and the end of the Madagascar Plan was announced on 10 February 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHildebrand200570_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHildebrand200570-124">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_during_World_War_II" title="History of the Jews during World War II">History of the Jews during World War II</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="German-occupied_Poland">German-occupied Poland</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Occupation_of_Poland_1939_(b%26w).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Occupation_of_Poland_1939_%28b%26w%29.png/260px-Occupation_of_Poland_1939_%28b%26w%29.png" width="260" height="352" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Occupation_of_Poland_1939_%28b%26w%29.png/390px-Occupation_of_Poland_1939_%28b%26w%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Occupation_of_Poland_1939_%28b%26w%29.png/520px-Occupation_of_Poland_1939_%28b%26w%29.png 2x" data-file-width="2481" data-file-height="3355" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Occupation_of_Poland_1939_(b%26w).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Polish_areas_annexed_by_Nazi_Germany" title="Polish areas annexed by Nazi Germany">Polish areas annexed by Nazi Germany</a>, and the USSR, with <a href="/wiki/General_Government" title="General Government">General Government</a> territory in the middle, 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Poland" title="The Holocaust in Poland">The Holocaust in Poland</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">Invasion of Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Poland_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Occupation of Poland (1939–1945)">Occupation of Poland (1939–1945)</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland" title="History of the Jews in Poland">History of the Jews in Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jewish_ghettos_in_German-occupied_Poland" title="Jewish ghettos in German-occupied Poland">Jewish ghettos in German-occupied Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/General_Government" title="General Government">General Government</a></div>
<p>When Germany <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">invaded Poland</a>, it gained control of about 2 million Jews in the occupied territory. The rest of Poland was <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_Poland_annexed_by_the_Soviet_Union#Soviet_occupation_of_Poland.2C_1939.E2.80.931941" title="Territories of Poland annexed by the Soviet Union">occupied by the Soviet Union</a>, which gained control of the rest of Poland's pre-war population of 3.3 to 3.5 million Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrowe2008158.E2.80.93159_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrowe2008158.E2.80.93159-125">[117]</a></sup> German plans for Poland included expelling gentile Poles from large areas, the confining of Jews, and settling Germans on the emptied lands. To help the process along, <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich" title="Reinhard Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a>, head of the <a href="/wiki/Reich_Security_Main_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Reich Security Main Office">Reich Security Main Office</a>, ordered that the "leadership class" in Poland must be killed and the Jews expelled from the <a href="/wiki/Polish_areas_annexed_by_Nazi_Germany" title="Polish areas annexed by Nazi Germany">Polish areas annexed by Nazi Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016136.E2.80.93137_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016136.E2.80.93137-126">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Germans initiated a policy of sending Jews from all territories they had recently annexed (<a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> and western Poland) to the central section of Poland, which they called the <a href="/wiki/General_Government" title="General Government">General Government</a>. There the Jews were concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Ghettos_in_Nazi-occupied_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghettos in Nazi-occupied Europe">ghettos</a> in major cities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201629_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201629-127">[119]</a></sup> Cities chosen were located on railway lines in order to facilitate later deportation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning2004111.E2.80.93113_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning2004111.E2.80.93113-128">[120]</a></sup> Food supplies were restricted and public hygiene was difficult. The inhabitants were subjected to <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced labour">forced labour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201629.E2.80.9330_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201629.E2.80.9330-129">[121]</a></sup> In the labour camps and ghettos at least half a million Jews died of starvation, diseases, and poor living conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016146_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016146-130">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ghettos were not initially considered a step along the way towards the extermination of the Jews. Instead, they were one step towards a policy of creating a territorial reservation used to contain Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201631_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201631-131">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lublin_Reservation">Lublin Reservation</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lublin_Reservation" title="Lublin Reservation">Lublin Reservation</a></div>
<p>After the invasion of Poland, the Germans planned to set up a "Jewish reservation" in the <a href="/wiki/Lublin_Ghetto" title="Lublin Ghetto">Lublin</a> district of the <a href="/wiki/General_Government" title="General Government">General Government</a> territory.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016264_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016264-132">[124]</a></sup> Adolf Eichmann was assigned the task of removing all Jews from Germany, Austria, and the <a href="/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia" title="Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia">Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia</a> to this reservation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani200477.E2.80.9379_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani200477.E2.80.9379-133">[125]</a></sup> The first short-term plan to be implemented was to concentrate the Jews around Nisko.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGerlach201660_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGerlach201660-134">[126]</a></sup> Deportations began in October 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000153_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000153-135">[127]</a></sup> Although this "<a href="/wiki/Nisko_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Nisko Plan">Nisko Plan</a>" initially intended to remove 80,000 Jews from the so-called Greater German Reich, Eichmann managed to send only 4,700 Jews to Nisko as of March 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2004259.2C_280.2C_288_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2004259.2C_280.2C_288-136">[128]</a></sup> By that time 95,000 Jews chiefly from Poland were already deported to this area,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013133_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013133-137">[129]</a></sup> most of them before the end of February. They were pressed to work in the RSHA camps of <i><a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Generalplan Ost</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdelheit199452_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdelheit199452-138">[130]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Nisko Plan was put on hold in late March,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000154_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000154-139">[131]</a></sup> and scrapped in April 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016260_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016260-140">[132]</a></sup> By mid-October however, the idea of a "Jewish reservation" was revived by Himmler,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016262_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016262-141">[133]</a></sup> due to the influx of <a href="/wiki/Volksdeutsche" title="Volksdeutsche">Germanic settlers</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Warthegau" class="mw-redirect" title="Warthegau">Warthegau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016261.E2.80.93263_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016261.E2.80.93263-142">[134]</a></sup> Resettlement actions connected to this plan continued until January 1941 under <a href="/wiki/Odilo_Globocnik" title="Odilo Globocnik">Globocnik</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2004266_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2004266-143">[135]</a></sup> and included both Jews and Poles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010156-159_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010156-159-144">[136]</a></sup> Some 51 camps were created,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[137]</a></sup> but further plans of deporting up to 600,000 additional Jews to the <a href="/wiki/Lublin_reservation" class="mw-redirect" title="Lublin reservation">Lublin reservation</a> failed because of logistical and political factors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016262_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016262-141">[133]</a></sup> Notably, the Lublin district known for its <a href="/wiki/Polesie_National_Park" title="Polesie National Park">swampy nature</a>, in less than two years would lend itself to the industrialized murder of hundreds of thousands of Jews during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Reinhard" title="Operation Reinhard">Operation Reinhard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990160_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990160-146">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_occupied_countries">Other occupied countries</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Norway" title="The Holocaust in Norway">The Holocaust in Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rescue_of_the_Danish_Jews" title="Rescue of the Danish Jews">Rescue of the Danish Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Belgium" title="The Holocaust in Belgium">The Holocaust in Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Luxembourg" title="The Holocaust in Luxembourg">The Holocaust in Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_France" title="The Holocaust in France">The Holocaust in France</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Serbia" title="The Holocaust in Serbia">The Holocaust in Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_the_Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="The Holocaust in the Independent State of Croatia">The Holocaust in the Independent State of Croatia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Italian_Libya" class="mw-redirect" title="The Holocaust in Italian Libya">The Holocaust in Italian Libya</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:German_J_stamped_passport_used_to_escape_Europe_in_1940.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/German_J_stamped_passport_used_to_escape_Europe_in_1940.jpg/170px-German_J_stamped_passport_used_to_escape_Europe_in_1940.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/German_J_stamped_passport_used_to_escape_Europe_in_1940.jpg/255px-German_J_stamped_passport_used_to_escape_Europe_in_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/German_J_stamped_passport_used_to_escape_Europe_in_1940.jpg/340px-German_J_stamped_passport_used_to_escape_Europe_in_1940.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1287" data-file-height="1928" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:German_J_stamped_passport_used_to_escape_Europe_in_1940.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German "J" stamped passport used to escape Europe in 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Germany <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Campaign" title="Norwegian Campaign">invaded Norway</a> in April 1940. The country was completely occupied by June.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016169_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016169-147">[139]</a></sup> There were about 1,800 Jews in Norway, persecuted by the Norwegian Nazis. In late 1940, the Jews were banned from some occupations and in 1941 all Jews had to register their property with the government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002162_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002162-148">[140]</a></sup> Also in 1940, <a href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_Denmark_(1940)" title="German invasion of Denmark (1940)">Germany invaded Denmark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016169_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016169-147">[139]</a></sup> The country was overrun so quickly that there was no chance of organizing resistance. Consequently, the Danish government stayed in power and the Germans found it easier to work through it. Because of this, few measures were taken against the Danish Jews before 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002161_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002161-149">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Germans <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Netherlands" title="Battle of the Netherlands">invaded the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">France</a> in May 1940. In the Netherlands, the Germans installed <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Seyss-Inquart" title="Arthur Seyss-Inquart">Arthur Seyss-Inquart</a> as <i><a href="/wiki/Reichskommissar" title="Reichskommissar">Reichskommissar</a></i>, who quickly began to persecute the approximately 140,000 Dutch Jews. Jews were forced out of their jobs and had to register with the government. Non-Jewish Dutch citizens protested these measures and in February 1941 staged a strike that was quickly crushed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002162.E2.80.93163_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002162.E2.80.93163-150">[142]</a></sup> After Belgium's surrender at the end of May 1940, it was ruled by a German military governor, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Falkenhausen" title="Alexander von Falkenhausen">Alexander von Falkenhausen</a>, which enacted anti-Jewish measures against the approximately 90,000 Jews in Belgium, many of whom were refugees from Germany or Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002164_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002164-151">[143]</a></sup> France had approximately 300,000 Jews, divided between the German-occupied northern part of France, and the unoccupied collaborationist southern areas under the <a href="/wiki/Vichy_regime" class="mw-redirect" title="Vichy regime">Vichy regime</a>. The occupied regions were under the control of a military governor, and there, anti-Jewish measures were not enacted as quickly as they were in the Vichy-controlled areas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002165.E2.80.93166_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002165.E2.80.93166-152">[144]</a></sup> In July 1940, the Jews in the parts of <a href="/wiki/Alsace-Lorraine" title="Alsace-Lorraine">Alsace-Lorraine</a> that had been annexed to Germany were expelled into Vichy France.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZuccotti199352_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZuccotti199352-153">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Yugoslavia" title="Invasion of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Greece" title="Battle of Greece">Greece</a> were invaded in April 1941, and both countries surrendered before the end of the month. Germany and Italy divided Greece into occupation zones, but did not eliminate it as a country. Yugoslavia was dismembered, with regions in the north being annexed by Germany and regions along the coast were made part of Italy. The rest of the country was divided into a <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">puppet state of Croatia</a>, which was nominally an ally of Germany, and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, which was governed by a combination of military and police administrators. There were approximately 80,000 Jews in Yugoslavia when it was invaded. The ruling party in <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ustashe" class="mw-redirect" title="Ustashe">Ustashe</a>, not only killed Jews, but also murdered and expelled Orthodox Christian Serbs and Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002192.E2.80.93193_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002192.E2.80.93193-154">[146]</a></sup> One difference between the Germans and the Croatians was the fact that the Ustashe allowed its Jewish and Serbian victims to convert to Catholicism so they could escape death. Serbia was declared free of Jews in August 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016134_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016134-155">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Germany's_allies"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany.27s_allies">Germany's allies</span></h3>
<p>Germany's ally <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> introduced some antisemitic measures, but there was less antisemitism than there was in Germany. Italian-occupied countries were generally safer for Jews than German-occupied territories. In some areas, the Italian authorities even attempted to protect Jews, such as in the Croatian areas of the Balkans. But while Italian forces in Russia were not as vicious towards Jews as the Germans, they did not try to stop German atrocities either. There were no deportations of Italian Jews to Germany while Italy remained an ally.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016137.E2.80.93139_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016137.E2.80.93139-156">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> was pressured to give the Germans its Jews (who numbered around 200) in 1942, but given the opposition among the people and government, this did not happen. Eight non-Finnish Jews were deported in late 1942,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[i]</a></sup> but that was the only case. Finnish Jews even fought in the army during the period it was allied with Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016140_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016140-157">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a> had little antisemitism in its society, and did not persecute Jews in most of the territories it controlled. Jews in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> were confined, but despite German pressure, they were not killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016141_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016141-159">[150]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg/220px-%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg/330px-%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg/440px-%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="939" data-file-height="675" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pulling dead bodies out of a moving death train carrying Romanian Jews from the <a href="/wiki/Jassy_pogrom" class="mw-redirect" title="Jassy pogrom">Jassy pogrom</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> implemented a number of anti-Jewish measures in May and June 1940 as part of its efforts towards an alliance with Germany. These included forcing Jews from government service and relegation to the status of second-class citizens. Pogroms were also carried out and by March 1941, Jewish property had been confiscated and all Jews lost their jobs. After Romania joined the invasion of the Soviet Union in June 1941, Romanian troops carried out massacres in Romanian-controlled territory, including the <a href="/wiki/1941_Odessa_massacre" title="1941 Odessa massacre">Odessa massacre</a> of 20,000 Jews in Odessa in late 1941. Romania also set up concentration camps under its control in <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a>, where approximately 154,000 to 170,000 Jews were deported from 1941 to 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016131.E2.80.93133_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016131.E2.80.93133-160">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>Anti-Jewish measures similar to those in Germany were introduced in <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> which would later deport its Jews to German concentration and extermination camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016134.E2.80.93135_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016134.E2.80.93135-161">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> introduced some anti-Jewish measures in 1940 and 1941, including the requirement to wear a yellow star, the banning of mixed marriages, and the loss of property.
