Bulgaria annexed <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a> and Macedonia, and in February 1943 agreed to deport 20,000 Jews to <a href="/wiki/Treblinka_extermination_camp" title="Treblinka extermination camp">Treblinka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013161_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013161-162">[153]</a></sup> All Jews from the annexed territories were sent off to their deaths, amounting to 11,000 men, women and children, therefore plans were made to deport additional 6,000–8,000 Bulgarian Jews from Sofia in order to meet the quota.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013161_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013161-162">[153]</a></sup> When the plans became public, the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church</a> and many Bulgarians protested, and King <a href="/wiki/Boris_III_of_Bulgaria" title="Boris III of Bulgaria">Boris III</a> cancelled the deportation of Jews native to Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016136.E2.80.93137_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016136.E2.80.93137-163">[154]</a></sup> Instead, they were expelled to the interior, pending further decision.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013161_162-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013161-162">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> expelled Jews who were not Hungarian citizens from its newly annexed lands in 1941, it did not deport most of the Hungarian Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016135_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016135-164">[155]</a></sup> In Budapest, nearly 80,000 Jews were killed by the Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Arrow_Cross_Party" title="Arrow Cross Party">Arrow Cross battalions</a> in late 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013274_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERozettSpector2013274-165">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several forced labor camps for Jews were established in <a href="/wiki/Italian_Libya" title="Italian Libya">Italian-controlled Libya</a>. Almost 2600 <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Libya" title="History of the Jews in Libya">Libyan Jews</a> were sent to camps, where 562 died.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[157]</a></sup> Vichy France's government implemented anti-Jewish measures in <a href="/wiki/French_Algeria" title="French Algeria">French Algeria</a> and the two French Protectorates of <a href="/wiki/French_Protectorate_of_Tunisia" class="mw-redirect" title="French Protectorate of Tunisia">Tunisia</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_protectorate_in_Morocco" title="French protectorate in Morocco">Morocco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer2001256.E2.80.93257_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer2001256.E2.80.93257-167">[158]</a></sup> Tunisia had 85,000 Jews when the Germans and Italians arrived in November 1942. An estimated 5,000 Jews were subjected to forced labor.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Concentration_and_labor_camps">Concentration and labor camps</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nazi_concentration_camps" title="List of Nazi concentration camps">List of Nazi concentration camps</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Extermination_through_labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Extermination through labor">Extermination through labor</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Birkenau_Extermination_Camp_-_Oswiecim,_Poland_-_NARA_-_305904.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Birkenau_Extermination_Camp_-_Oswiecim%2C_Poland_-_NARA_-_305904.jpg/220px-Birkenau_Extermination_Camp_-_Oswiecim%2C_Poland_-_NARA_-_305904.jpg" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Birkenau_Extermination_Camp_-_Oswiecim%2C_Poland_-_NARA_-_305904.jpg/330px-Birkenau_Extermination_Camp_-_Oswiecim%2C_Poland_-_NARA_-_305904.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Birkenau_Extermination_Camp_-_Oswiecim%2C_Poland_-_NARA_-_305904.jpg/440px-Birkenau_Extermination_Camp_-_Oswiecim%2C_Poland_-_NARA_-_305904.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2443" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Birkenau_Extermination_Camp_-_Oswiecim,_Poland_-_NARA_-_305904.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial photograph of Auschwitz–Birkenau taken by a surveillance plane, 13 September 1944.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Third Reich first used concentration camps as places of unlawful incarceration of political opponents and so-called 'enemies of the State'. Large numbers of Jews were sent there after the <i>Kristallnacht</i> of 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaumel2001135_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaumel2001135-169">[160]</a></sup> The camps were not designed to be killing centers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel201050.E2.80.9352_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel201050.E2.80.9352-170">[161]</a></sup> After the start of the war, new camp complexes were established, and some were located outside Germany in occupied Europe. The number of prisoners continued to soar, from about 80,000 in 1942, to 700,000 in January 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-Straede_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Straede-171">[162]</a></sup> Most wartime prisoners of the camps were not Germans, but members of other nationalities under the control of the Third Reich.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015287.E2.80.93288_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015287.E2.80.93288-172">[163]</a></sup> It is estimated that in occupied countries the Nazis had established 30,000 slave labor camps and subcamps, almost 1,000 concentration camps, and another 1,000 prisoner-of-war camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELichtblau2013_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELichtblau2013-173">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>After 1942, the economic functions of the camps, previously secondary to their penal and terror functions, came to the fore. Forced labour of camp prisoners became commonplace and companies utilized cheap prisoner labour.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaumel2001135_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaumel2001135-169">[160]</a></sup> The guards became much more brutal, and the death rate increased markedly as the guards not only beat and starved prisoners, but also killed them more frequently.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015287.E2.80.93288_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015287.E2.80.93288-172">[163]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Extermination_through_labour" title="Extermination through labour">Extermination through labour</a> was a policy of systematic extermination—camp inmates would literally be worked to death, or worked to physical exhaustion, when they would be gassed or shot.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010314.E2.80.93320_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010314.E2.80.93320-174">[165]</a></sup> For many prisoners, the Germans estimated the average life span in a concentration camp at three months, mainly due to lack of food and clothing, constant epidemics, and frequent punishments for the most minor transgressions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201676_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201676-175">[166]</a></sup> The shifts were long and often involved exposure to dangerous materials. Safety was neglected.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016104_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016104-176">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prisoner transportation between camps was often carried out in freight cars with the prisoners packed very tightly. Long delays often took place, with the prisoners confined in the cars on sidings for days.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERozett19901222_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERozett19901222-177">[168]</a></sup> In mid-1942 labour camps began requiring newly arrived prisoners to be put into quarantine for four weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015347_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015347-178">[169]</a></sup> Some camps <a href="/wiki/Identification_in_Nazi_camps" title="Identification in Nazi camps">tattooed prisoners</a> with an identification number on arrival, but not all did.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarran2000461_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarran2000461-179">[170]</a></sup> Prisoners also had <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camp_badge" title="Nazi concentration camp badge">colored triangles</a> on their uniforms, with the color of the triangle denoting the reason for their incarceration.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[j]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015119_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015119-186">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ghettos">Ghettos</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ghettos_in_Nazi-occupied_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghettos in Nazi-occupied Europe">Ghettos in Nazi-occupied Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jewish_ghettos_in_German-occupied_Poland" title="Jewish ghettos in German-occupied Poland">Jewish ghettos in German-occupied Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nazi-era_ghettos" title="List of Nazi-era ghettos">List of Nazi-era ghettos</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Transfer_of_the_dead_Warsaw_Ghetto_August_1941.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Transfer_of_the_dead_Warsaw_Ghetto_August_1941.jpg/220px-Transfer_of_the_dead_Warsaw_Ghetto_August_1941.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Transfer_of_the_dead_Warsaw_Ghetto_August_1941.jpg/330px-Transfer_of_the_dead_Warsaw_Ghetto_August_1941.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Transfer_of_the_dead_Warsaw_Ghetto_August_1941.jpg/440px-Transfer_of_the_dead_Warsaw_Ghetto_August_1941.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2642" data-file-height="1940" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Transfer_of_the_dead_Warsaw_Ghetto_August_1941.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carts with emaciated corpses collected daily in the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto" title="Warsaw Ghetto">Warsaw Ghetto</a>, August 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dd><i>Main ghettos: <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82ystok_Ghetto" title="Białystok Ghetto">Białystok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Ghetto" title="Budapest Ghetto">Budapest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Ghetto" title="Kraków Ghetto">Kraków</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kovno_Ghetto" title="Kovno Ghetto">Kovno</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA_Ghetto" title="Łódź Ghetto">Łódź</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lw%C3%B3w_Ghetto" title="Lwów Ghetto">Lvov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riga_Ghetto" title="Riga Ghetto">Riga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vilna_Ghetto" title="Vilna Ghetto">Vilna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto" title="Warsaw Ghetto">Warsaw</a>.</i></dd>
</dl>
<p>After invading Poland, the Germans established ghettos in the incorporated territories and General Government to confine Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201629_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201629-127">[119]</a></sup> The ghettos were formed and closed off from the outside world at different times and for different reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning1986345.E2.80.93348_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning1986345.E2.80.93348-187">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg2003216.E2.80.937_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg2003216.E2.80.937-188">[178]</a></sup> For example, the Łódź ghetto was closed in April 1940,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201629_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201629-127">[119]</a></sup> to force the Jews inside to give up money and valuables;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990166_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990166-189">[179]</a></sup> the Warsaw ghetto was closed for health considerations (for the people outside, not inside, the ghetto),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990169_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990169-190">[180]</a></sup> but this did not happen until November 1940;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201629_127-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201629-127">[119]</a></sup> and the Kraków ghetto was not established until March 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010161_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010161-191">[181]</a></sup> The Warsaw Ghetto contained 380,000 people<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201629_127-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201629-127">[119]</a></sup> and was the largest ghetto in Poland; the Łódź Ghetto was the second largest,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010167_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010167-192">[182]</a></sup> holding between 160,000<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990165_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990165-193">[183]</a></sup> to 223,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016148_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016148-194">[184]</a></sup> Because of the long drawn-out process of establishing ghettos, it is unlikely that they were originally considered part of a systematic attempt to eliminate Jews completely.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010166_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010166-195">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Germans required each ghetto to be run by a <i><a href="/wiki/Judenrat" title="Judenrat">Judenrat</a></i>, or Jewish council.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrunk19961.E2.80.936_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrunk19961.E2.80.936-196">[186]</a></sup> Councils were responsible for a ghetto's day-to-day operations, including distributing food, water, heat, medical care, and shelter. The Germans also required councils to confiscate property, organize forced labor, and, finally, facilitate deportations to extermination camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg1995106_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg1995106-197">[187]</a></sup> The councils' basic strategy was one of trying to minimise losses, by cooperating with German authorities, bribing officials, and petitioning for better conditions or clemency.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg1995170_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg1995170-198">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eventually the Germans ordered the councils to compile lists of names of deportees to be sent for "resettlement".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016150.E2.80.93152_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016150.E2.80.93152-199">[189]</a></sup> Although most ghetto councils complied with these orders,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg1980104_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg1980104-200">[190]</a></sup> many councils tried to send the least useful workers or those unable to work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016150.E2.80.93151_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016150.E2.80.93151-201">[191]</a></sup> Leaders who refused these orders were shot. Some individuals or even complete councils committed suicide rather than cooperate with the deportations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum200681.E2.80.9383_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum200681.E2.80.9383-202">[192]</a></sup> Others, like <a href="/wiki/Chaim_Rumkowski" title="Chaim Rumkowski">Chaim Rumkowski</a>, who became the "dedicated autocrat" of Łódź,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg1995109_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg1995109-203">[193]</a></sup> argued that their responsibility was to save the Jews who could be saved, and that therefore others had to be sacrificed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum200679.E2.80.9381_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum200679.E2.80.9381-204">[194]</a></sup> The councils' actions in facilitating Germany's persecution and murder of ghetto inhabitants was important to the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg20031111_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg20031111-205">[195]</a></sup> When cooperation crumbled, as happened in the Warsaw ghetto after the Jewish Combat Organisation displaced the council's authority, the Germans lost control.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010285_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010285-206">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ghettos were intended to be temporary until the Jews were deported to other locations, which never happened. Instead, the inhabitants were sent to extermination camps. The ghettos were, in effect, immensely crowded prisons serving as instruments of "slow, passive murder."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006114_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006114-207">[197]</a></sup> Though the Warsaw Ghetto contained 30% of Warsaw's population, it occupied only 2.5% of the city's area, averaging over 9 people per room.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003239_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003239-208">[198]</a></sup> Between 1940 and 1942, starvation and disease, especially <a href="/wiki/Typhoid_fever" title="Typhoid fever">typhoid</a>, killed many in the ghettos.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003242.E2.80.93243_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003242.E2.80.93243-209">[199]</a></sup> Over 43,000 Warsaw ghetto residents, or one in ten of the total population, died in 1941;<sup id="cite_ref-USHMMDepoWar_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USHMMDepoWar-210">[200]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Theresienstadt" class="mw-redirect" title="Theresienstadt">Theresienstadt</a>, more than half the residents died in 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006114_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006114-207">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>Himmler ordered the closing of ghettos in Poland in mid-July 1942, with most inhabitants going to extermination camps. Those Jews needed for war production would be confined at concentration camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990378_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990378-211">[201]</a></sup> The deportations from the Warsaw Ghetto began on 22 July; over the almost two months of the <i>Aktion</i>, until 12 September, the Warsaw ghetto went from approximately 350,000 inhabitants to about 65,000. Those deported were <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_trains" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust trains">transported in freight trains</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Treblinka_extermination_camp" title="Treblinka extermination camp">Treblinka extermination camp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990378.E2.80.93380_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990378.E2.80.93380-212">[202]</a></sup> Similar deportations happened in other ghettos, with many ghettos totally emptied.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990382.E2.80.93385_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990382.E2.80.93385-213">[203]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lviv_pogrom_(June_-_July_1941).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lviv_pogrom_%28June_-_July_1941%29.jpg/170px-Lviv_pogrom_%28June_-_July_1941%29.jpg" width="170" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lviv_pogrom_%28June_-_July_1941%29.jpg/255px-Lviv_pogrom_%28June_-_July_1941%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lviv_pogrom_%28June_-_July_1941%29.jpg/340px-Lviv_pogrom_%28June_-_July_1941%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="438" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lviv_pogrom_(June_-_July_1941).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jewish woman chased by men and youth armed with clubs during the <a href="/wiki/Lviv_pogroms" title="Lviv pogroms">Lviv pogroms</a>, July 1941, then <a href="/wiki/Occupied_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupied Poland">occupied Poland</a>, now Ukraine</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Ghetto_uprising" title="Ghetto uprising">ghetto uprisings</a> occurred in mid-1942 in small community ghettos.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990474.E2.80.93478_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990474.E2.80.93478-214">[204]</a></sup> Although there were armed resistance attempts in both the larger and smaller ghettos in 1943, in every case they failed against the overwhelming German military force, and the remaining Jews were either killed or deported to the death camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006175.E2.80.93177_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006175.E2.80.93177-215">[205]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pogroms">Pogroms</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">Pogrom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dorohoi_Pogrom" class="mw-redirect" title="Dorohoi Pogrom">Dorohoi Pogrom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ia%C5%9Fi_pogrom" class="mw-redirect" title="Iaşi pogrom">Iaşi pogrom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jedwabne_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Jedwabne Massacre">Jedwabne Massacre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legionnaires%27_Rebellion_and_Bucharest_Pogrom" class="mw-redirect" title="Legionnaires' Rebellion and Bucharest Pogrom">Legionnaires' Rebellion and Bucharest Pogrom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lviv_pogroms" title="Lviv pogroms">Lviv pogroms</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1941_Odessa_massacre" title="1941 Odessa massacre">1941 Odessa massacre</a></div>
<p>A number of deadly pogroms occurred during the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990163.2C_258_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990163.2C_258-216">[206]</a></sup> The Germans encouraged some and others were spontaneous.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016195_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016195-217">[207]</a></sup> Some, such as the <a href="/wiki/Ia%C5%9Fi_pogrom" class="mw-redirect" title="Iaşi pogrom">Iaşi pogrom</a>, were in lands controlled by Germany's allies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003267.E2.80.93269_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003267.E2.80.93269-218">[208]</a></sup> In the series of <a href="/wiki/Lviv_pogroms" title="Lviv pogroms">Lviv pogroms</a> committed in <a href="/wiki/Occupied_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupied Poland">occupied Poland</a>, perhaps initiated by the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ukrainian_Nationalists" title="Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists">Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists</a>, some 6,000 <a href="/wiki/Polish_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Jews">Polish Jews</a> were murdered in the streets in July 1941, on top of 3,000 arrests and mass shootings by <i>Einsatzgruppe C</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010194_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010194-219">[209]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Jedwabne_pogrom" title="Jedwabne pogrom">Jedwabne pogrom</a> of July 1941, in the presence of the German officers, several hundred Jews were murdered by some local Poles, with some being burned alive in a barn.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010196_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010196-220">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[k]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_squads">Death squads</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Ukraine" title="The Holocaust in Ukraine">The Holocaust in Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Lithuania" title="The Holocaust in Lithuania">The Holocaust in Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Latvia" title="The Holocaust in Latvia">The Holocaust in Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Estonia" title="The Holocaust in Estonia">The Holocaust in Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Belarus" title="The Holocaust in Belarus">The Holocaust in Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Russia" title="The Holocaust in Russia">The Holocaust in Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mass_graves_in_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass graves in the Soviet Union">Mass graves in the Soviet Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_crimes_of_the_Wehrmacht" title="War crimes of the Wehrmacht">War crimes of the Wehrmacht</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Collaboration_with_the_Axis_Powers_during_World_War_II" title="Collaboration with the Axis Powers during World War II">Collaboration with the Axis Powers during World War II</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Babi_Yar" title="Babi Yar">Babi Yar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rumbula_massacre" title="Rumbula massacre">Rumbula massacre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kamianets-Podilskyi_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Kamianets-Podilskyi Massacre">Kamianets-Podilskyi Massacre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ponary_massacre" title="Ponary massacre">Ponary massacre</a></div>
<p>Germany invaded the Soviet Union in June 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans198959_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans198959-222">[211]</a></sup> German propaganda portrayed the war against the Soviet Union as both an ideological war between German National Socialism and Jewish Bolshevism and a racial war between the Germans and the Jewish, Romani and Slavic <i><a href="/wiki/Untermenschen" class="mw-redirect" title="Untermenschen">Untermenschen</a></i> ("sub-humans").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurleigh2001512.2C_526.E2.80.93527_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurleigh2001512.2C_526.E2.80.93527-223">[212]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Einsatzgruppe_shooting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Einsatzgruppe_shooting.jpg/220px-Einsatzgruppe_shooting.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Einsatzgruppe_shooting.jpg/330px-Einsatzgruppe_shooting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Einsatzgruppe_shooting.jpg/440px-Einsatzgruppe_shooting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="406" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Einsatzgruppe_shooting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German police shooting women and children from the <a href="/wiki/Mizocz_Ghetto" title="Mizocz Ghetto">Mizocz Ghetto</a>, 14 October 1942</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Local populations in some occupied Soviet territories actively participated in the killings of Jews and others. Besides participating in killings and pogroms, they helped identify Jews for persecution and rounded up Jews for German actions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004268_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004268-224">[213]</a></sup> German involvement ranged from active instigation and involvement to more generalized guidance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004275_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004275-225">[214]</a></sup> In Lithuania, Latvia, and western Ukraine locals were deeply involved in the murder of Jews from the beginning of the German occupation. Some of these Latvian and Lithuanian units also participated in the murder of Jews in Belarus. In the south, Ukrainians killed about 24,000 Jews and some went to Poland to serve as concentration and death-camp guards.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004268_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004268-224">[213]</a></sup> Military units from some countries allied to Germany also killed Jews. Romanian units were given orders to exterminate and wipe out Jews in areas they controlled.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004275.E2.80.93276_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004275.E2.80.93276-226">[215]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e_militia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ustaše militia">Ustaše militia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">Croatia</a> persecuted and murdered Jews, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016134_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016134-155">[147]</a></sup> Many of the killings were carried out in public, a change from previous practice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004270.E2.80.93271_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatth.C3.A4us2004270.E2.80.93271-227">[216]</a></sup></p>
<p>The mass killings of Jews in the occupied Soviet territories was assigned to four SS formations called <i><a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a></i> ("task groups"), which were under Heydrich's overall command. Similar formations had been used to a limited extent in Poland in 1939, but the ones operating in the Soviet territories were much larger.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning2004224.E2.80.93225_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning2004224.E2.80.93225-228">[217]</a></sup> The <i>Einsatzgruppen'</i>s commanders were ordinary citizens: the great majority were professionals and most were intellectuals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg2003291_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg2003291-229">[218]</a></sup> By the winter of 1941–1942, the four <i>Einsatzgruppen</i> and their helpers had killed almost 500,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel202067_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel202067-230">[219]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg/220px-Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg/330px-Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg/440px-Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="319" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Liep%C4%81ja_massacres" title="Liepāja massacres">mass murder of 2,749 Jews on the beach near the city of Liepāja</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, on 15–17 December 1941.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The largest massacre of Jews by the mobile killing squads in the Soviet Union was at a ravine called <a href="/wiki/Babi_Yar" title="Babi Yar">Babi Yar</a> outside <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016199.E2.80.93200_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016199.E2.80.93200-231">[220]</a></sup> where 33,771 Jews were killed in a single operation on 29–30 September 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008226.E2.80.93227_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008226.E2.80.93227-232">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[l]</a></sup> A mixture of SS and Security Police, assisted by Ukrainian police, carried out the killings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002203_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002203-235">[223]</a></sup> Although they did not actively participate in the killings, men of the <a href="/wiki/6th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="6th Army (Wehrmacht)">6th Army</a> helped round up the Jews of Kiev and transport them to be shot.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritz2011102.E2.80.93104_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritz2011102.E2.80.93104-236">[224]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the end of the war, estimates of the number of victims of the <i>Einsatzgruppen</i> and their helpers in the local population and the German Army are about 2 million. Of those, about 1.3 million were Jews and perhaps as many as quarter million were Roma.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016200_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016200-237">[225]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gas_vans">Gas vans</span></h3>
<p>As the mass shootings continued in Russia, the Germans began to search for new methods of mass murder. This was driven by a need to have a more efficient method than simply shooting millions of victims. Himmler also feared that the mass shootings were causing psychological problems in the SS. His concerns were shared by his subordinates in the field.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199842.E2.80.9343_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199842.E2.80.9343-238">[226]</a></sup> In December 1939 and January 1940, another method besides shooting was tried. Experimental <a href="/wiki/Gas_van" title="Gas van">gas vans</a> equipped with gas cylinders and a sealed compartment were used to kill the disabled and mentally-ill in <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Poland_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Occupation of Poland (1939–1945)">occupied Poland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016160_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016160-239">[227]</a></sup> Similar vans, but using the exhaust fumes rather than bottled gas, were introduced to the <a href="/wiki/Che%C5%82mno_extermination_camp" title="Chełmno extermination camp">Chełmno extermination camp</a> in December 1941,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGerlach201674_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGerlach201674-240">[228]</a></sup> and some were used by in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">occupied Soviet Union</a>, for example in smaller clearing actions in the <a href="/wiki/Minsk_ghetto" class="mw-redirect" title="Minsk ghetto">Minsk ghetto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016513_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016513-241">[229]</a></sup> They also were used for murder in Yugoslavia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad2009138_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad2009138-242">[230]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_Solution">Final Solution</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jew_Killings_in_Ivangorod_(1942).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Jew_Killings_in_Ivangorod_%281942%29.jpg/220px-Jew_Killings_in_Ivangorod_%281942%29.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Jew_Killings_in_Ivangorod_%281942%29.jpg/330px-Jew_Killings_in_Ivangorod_%281942%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Jew_Killings_in_Ivangorod_%281942%29.jpg/440px-Jew_Killings_in_Ivangorod_%281942%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2528" data-file-height="1744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jew_Killings_in_Ivangorod_(1942).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Executions of Jews by German army mobile killing units (<i>Einsatzgruppen</i>) near <a href="/wiki/Ivanhorod" title="Ivanhorod">Ivanhorod</a>, now Ukraine. The photo was mailed from the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a> to Germany and intercepted by a member of <a href="/wiki/Polish_resistance_movement_in_World_War_II" title="Polish resistance movement in World War II">the Polish resistance</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Final_Solution" title="Final Solution">Final Solution</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wannsee_Conference">Wannsee Conference</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wannsee_Conference" title="Wannsee Conference">Wannsee Conference</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich" title="Reinhard Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a> convened the <a href="/wiki/Wannsee_Conference" title="Wannsee Conference">Wannsee Conference</a> on 20 January 1942 in Berlin's Wannsee suburb. It brought together German leaders, from the Nazi party and government departments responsible for policies linked to Jewish issues. The conference's initial purpose was to discuss plans for a comprehensive solution to the "Jewish question in Europe." Heydrich was put in overall charge of "final solution" throughout Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199845_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199845-243">[231]</a></sup> Heydrich meant for the conference to share information among the officials so they would all share responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010305_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010305-244">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p>A copy of the minutes survives, but on Heydrich's instructions, they were written in "euphemistic language" so the exact words used are not known.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010306_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010306-245">[233]</a></sup> But Heydrich announced that the immigration plan had been replaced by an approach of deporting Jews to the east. This was just a provisional solution leading up to a final solution that would involve some 11<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million Jews living not only in territories controlled by Germany, but throughout continental Europe and areas adjacent to it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010307_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010307-246">[234]</a></sup> There was little doubt what the solution was: "Heydrich also made it clear what was understood by the phrase 'Final Solution': the Jews were to be annihilated by a combination of forced labour and mass murder."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010308_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010308-247">[235]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extermination_camps">Extermination camps</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">Extermination camp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Reinhard" title="Operation Reinhard">Operation Reinhard</a></div>
<p>Killing on a mass scale with gas as the main killing means is the main difference between a death or extermination camp and the rest of the German concentration and labour camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones2006153_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones2006153-248">[236]</a></sup> During 1942 three camps were built as extermination camps for <a href="/wiki/Operation_Reinhard" title="Operation Reinhard">Operation Reinhard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aktr_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aktr-249">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[m]</a></sup> About the same time, two other camps, <a href="/wiki/Che%C5%82mno_extermination_camp" title="Chełmno extermination camp">Chełmno</a><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[n]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Majdanek_concentration_camp" title="Majdanek concentration camp">Majdanek</a><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[o]</a></sup> which already existed had extermination facilities added to them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201669.E2.80.9371_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201669.E2.80.9371-259">[244]</a></sup> The three new camps were built for the sole purpose of killing large numbers of Jews as quickly as possible – at <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%82%C5%BCec_extermination_camp" title="Bełżec extermination camp">Bełżec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sobib%C3%B3r_extermination_camp" title="Sobibór extermination camp">Sobibór</a> and <a href="/wiki/Treblinka_extermination_camp" title="Treblinka extermination camp">Treblinka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201669_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201669-260">[245]</a></sup> At around the same time, Auschwitz, which was actually three camps, was experimenting with systematic killing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201671.E2.80.9372_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201671.E2.80.9372-261">[246]</a></sup> These six camps are generally considered to be death camps or extermination camps. A few other camps are occasionally also named as extermination camps, but there is no scholarly agreement on the additional camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel201057.E2.80.9358_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel201057.E2.80.9358-262">[247]</a></sup> Commonly mentioned as "other" death camps are <a href="/wiki/Mauthausen" title="Mauthausen">Mauthausen</a> in Austria<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel201057.E2.80.9358_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel201057.E2.80.9358-262">[247]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Stutthof" class="mw-redirect" title="Stutthof">Stutthof</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199881_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199881-263">[248]</a></sup> There may have been plans for camps at Mogilev and Lvov also, but they never progressed past the planning stage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010282_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010282-264">[249]</a></sup></p>
