<th align="left"><a href="/wiki/Treblinka_extermination_camp" title="Treblinka extermination camp">Treblinka</a></th>
<td align="right">870,000</td>
<td><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=The_Holocaust&amp;params=52_37_35_N_22_2_49_E_region:PL-49_type:landmark_source:GNIS&amp;title=Treblinka+%28Poland%29"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">52°37′35″N</span> <span class="longitude">22°2′49″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="vcard"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">52.62639°N 22.04694°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">52.62639; 22.04694</span></span><span style="display:none">﻿ (<span class="fn org">Treblinka (Poland)</span>)</span></span></span></a></span></td>
<td style="text-align:center;"><sup id="cite_ref-yvTreb_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yvTreb-272">[257]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gas_chambers">Gas chambers</span></h4>
<p>Usually, victims arrived by train.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199881.E2.80.9385_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199881.E2.80.9385-273">[258]</a></sup> Almost all arrivals at the Operation Reinhard camps of Treblinka, Sobibór, and Bełżec were sent directly to the gas chambers,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201669.E2.80.9370_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201669.E2.80.9370-274">[259]</a></sup> with occasional individuals selected to replace dead workers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrowe2008243_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrowe2008243-275">[260]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad198798_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad198798-276">[261]</a></sup> At Auschwitz, the camp officials usually subjected individuals to selections and some of new arrivals deemed fit to work were sent to slave labour.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199881.E2.80.9382_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199881.E2.80.9382-277">[262]</a></sup> Those selected for death at all camps were then told to undress and hand over their valuables to camp workers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003287.E2.80.93288_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003287.E2.80.93288-278">[263]</a></sup> They were then herded naked into the gas chambers. In order to prevent panic, the victims were often told these were showers or delousing chambers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b173_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b173-279">[264]</a></sup> The procedure at Chełmno was slightly different, as the victims were put into a mobile gas van and asphyxiated while being driven to prepared burial pits in the nearby forests. There the corpses were unloaded and buried.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMontague76.E2.80.9385_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontague76.E2.80.9385-280">[265]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Auschwitz, after the chambers were filled, the doors were shut and pellets of <a href="/wiki/Zyklon-B" class="mw-redirect" title="Zyklon-B">Zyklon-B</a> were dropped into the chambers through vents,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b162_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b162-281">[266]</a></sup> releasing toxic prussic acid, or <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_cyanide" title="Hydrogen cyanide">hydrogen cyanide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b157_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b157-282">[267]</a></sup> Those inside died within 20 minutes; the speed of death depended on how close the inmate was standing to a gas vent, according to the commandant <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_H%C3%B6ss" title="Rudolf Höss">Rudolf Höss</a>, who estimated that about one-third of the victims died immediately.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b170_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b170-283">[268]</a></sup> Johann Kremer, an SS doctor who oversaw the gassings, testified that: "Shouting and screaming of the victims could be heard through the opening and it was clear that they fought for their lives."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b163_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b163-284">[269]</a></sup> The gas was then pumped out, the bodies were removed, gold fillings in their teeth were extracted, and women's hair was cut.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b170.E2.80.93171_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b170.E2.80.93171-285">[270]</a></sup> The work was done by the <i><a href="/wiki/Sonderkommando" title="Sonderkommando">Sonderkommando</a>,</i> or work groups of Jewish prisoners.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b172_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b172-286">[271]</a></sup> At first at Auschwitz, the bodies were buried in deep pits and covered with lime, but between September and November 1942, on the orders of Himmler, they were dug up and burned. In early 1943, new gas chambers and crematoria were built to accommodate the numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b163.E2.80.93164_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiper1998b163.E2.80.93164-287">[272]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the three Reinhard camps the victims were killed by the exhaust fumes of stationary diesel engines.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201669.E2.80.9370_274-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201669.E2.80.9370-274">[259]</a></sup> Gold fillings were pulled from the corpses before burial, but the women's hair was cut before death. At Treblinka, in order to calm the arriving victims, the arrival platform was made to look like a train station, complete with fake clock.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199883.E2.80.9384_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199883.E2.80.9384-288">[273]</a></sup> Majdanek used Zyklon-B gas in its gas chambers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199884.E2.80.9385_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199884.E2.80.9385-289">[274]</a></sup> In contrast to Auschwitz, the three Reinhard camps were quite small.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010330_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010330-290">[275]</a></sup> At these camps, most of the initial victims were buried in pits, but in 1942 in order to hide the evidence of the extermination, the exhumation of the bodies and cremation of them was begun. Sobibór and Bełżec began the process in late 1942 but Treblinka did not start until March 1943. The bodies were burned in open fireplaces and the remaining bones were crushed into powder.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad1987170.E2.80.93171_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad1987170.E2.80.93171-291">[276]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jewish_resistance">Jewish resistance</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jewish_resistance_in_German-occupied_Europe" title="Jewish resistance in German-occupied Europe">Jewish resistance in German-occupied Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_13.jpg/170px-Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_13.jpg" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_13.jpg/255px-Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_13.jpg/340px-Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2138" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Captured members of the Jewish resistance, Warsaw Ghetto, 1943.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Peter_Longerich" title="Peter Longerich">Peter Longerich</a> observes that in ghettos in Poland by the end of 1942, "there was practically no resistance."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010340.E2.80.93341_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010340.E2.80.93341-292">[277]</a></sup> He argues that one of the reasons for this was that there were no organized groups until the early part of 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010341_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010341-293">[278]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Raul_Hilberg" title="Raul Hilberg">Raul Hilberg</a> accounts for this compliant attitude by evoking the <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jews" title="Persecution of Jews">history of Jewish persecution</a>: as had been the case before in history, simply appealing to their oppressors, and complying with orders, would hopefully avoid inflaming the situation and so mitigate the damage until the onslaught abated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg20031112.E2.80.931128_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg20031112.E2.80.931128-294">[279]</a></sup> They were "caught in the straitjacket of their history", and the realisation that this time was different came too late.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg20031112.E2.80.931128_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg20031112.E2.80.931128-294">[279]</a></sup></p>
<p>Discussing the case of Warsaw, Timothy Snyder notes in a similar vein that it was only during the three months after the massive deportations of July–September 1942 that general agreement on the need for armed resistance was reached.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010283_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010283-295">[280]</a></sup> By the time of the biggest act of armed resistance, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Ghetto uprising">Warsaw Ghetto uprising</a> of spring 1943, only a small minority of Polish Jews were still alive.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010341_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010341-293">[278]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Henri_Michel" title="Henri Michel">Henri Michel</a> argues that resistance consisted not only of physical opposition, but of any activity that gave the Jews dignity and humanity in humiliating and inhumane conditions. Yehuda Bauer restricts Michel's definition somewhat, making resistance as actions that opposed somehow the German directives, laws, or conduct.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer1997117_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer1997117-296">[281]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>In every ghetto, in every deportation train, in every labour camp, even in the death camps, the will to resist was strong, and took many forms: fighting with sticks and knives, individual acts of defiance and protest, the courage of obtaining food under the threat of death, the nobility of refusing to allow the Germans their final wish to gloat over panic and despair. Even passivity was a form of courage. ... To die with dignity was in itself courageous. To resist the dehumanizing, brutalizing force of evil, to refuse to be abased to the level of animals, to live through the torment, to outlive the tormentors, these too were courageous. Merely to give a witness by one's own testimony was, in the end, to contribute to a moral victory. Simply to survive was a victory of the human spirit.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— Martin Gilbert, <i>The Holocaust</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1985828_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1985828-297">[282]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>Hilberg cautions against overstating the extent of Jewish resistance, or using all-encompassing definitions of it like that deployed by Gilbert; arguing that by turning isolated incidents into resistance, it obscures the underlying German motivations and elevates the slaughter of innocent people into some kind of battle. He also contends that by ascribing to every European Jew acts of resistance, it diminishes the heroism of those who took active measures to resist the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg1996126.E2.80.93137_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg1996126.E2.80.93137-298">[283]</a></sup> Finally he asserts that the blending of the passive majority with the active few is a way of deflecting questions about the survival strategies and leadership of the Jewish community.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHilberg1996137_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHilberg1996137-299">[284]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_resistance">Armed resistance</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ghetto_Vilinus.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Ghetto_Vilinus.gif/220px-Ghetto_Vilinus.gif" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Ghetto_Vilinus.gif/330px-Ghetto_Vilinus.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Ghetto_Vilinus.gif/440px-Ghetto_Vilinus.gif 2x" data-file-width="472" data-file-height="346" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ghetto_Vilinus.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Armed members of the Jewish resistance, the <i><a href="/wiki/Fareynikte_Partizaner_Organizatsye" title="Fareynikte Partizaner Organizatsye">Fareynikte Partizaner Organizatsye</a></i>, active in the <a href="/wiki/Vilnius_Ghetto" class="mw-redirect" title="Vilnius Ghetto">Vilnius Ghetto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002219_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002219-300">[285]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jewish_resistance_in_German-occupied_Europe" title="Jewish resistance in German-occupied Europe">Organized uprisings</a> took place in at least 19 ghettos as well as some of the camps. Groups such as the Jewish Fighting Organization in the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto" title="Warsaw Ghetto">Warsaw Ghetto</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/United_Partisan_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="United Partisan Organization">United Partisan Organization</a> in Vilna, were formed to resist through armed revolts or resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201682.E2.80.9385_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201682.E2.80.9385-301">[286]</a></sup> Over a hundred revolts and uprisings are known to have occurred in ghettos and other locations in Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001291_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001291-302">[287]</a></sup></p>
<p>The best known example of Jewish armed resistance was the Warsaw Ghetto Uprising of 1943,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001291_302-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001291-302">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199894_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199894-303">[288]</a></sup> when around a thousand poorly armed Jewish fighters<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[p]</a></sup> held the SS off for four weeks before the German's superior forces defeated them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201683.E2.80.9384_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201683.E2.80.9384-306">[290]</a></sup> According to Polish and Jewish accounts, hundreds or thousands of Germans were killed,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGutman1994243_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGutman1994243-307">[291]</a></sup> while the Germans reported 16 dead.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016269_304-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016269-304">[289]</a></sup> The Germans reported around 14,000 Jews killed<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[q]</a></sup> and between 53,000<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016636_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016636-310">[293]</a></sup> and 56,000 deported.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016269_304-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016269-304">[289]</a></sup> A revolt in the Treblinka extermination camp occurred on 2 August 1943, when the inmates revolted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad1987286_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad1987286-311">[294]</a></sup> They killed five or six guards and set fire to a few camp buildings,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad1987293.E2.80.93294_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad1987293.E2.80.93294-312">[295]</a></sup> Of the approximately 850 prisoners in the camp,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad1987298_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad1987298-313">[296]</a></sup> only around 350 or so escaped the immediate area of the camp, and 70 of those survived the war.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[r]</a></sup> The camp itself was demolished soon after the revolt by the Germans, who used recaptured prisoners for the work before killing them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel198899_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel198899-315">[297]</a></sup> Another uprising occurred in the <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82ystok_Ghetto_Uprising" title="Białystok Ghetto Uprising">Białystok Ghettoon</a> 16 August 1943. The revolt began when the Germans announced mass deportations and a group of Jewish insurgents revolted. The fighting lasted five days, but the fighters were defeated by the superior numbers of the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199895.E2.80.9396_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199895.E2.80.9396-316">[298]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 October 1943, Jewish prisoners in Sobibór, including Jewish Soviet prisoners of war, attempted an escape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199898_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199898-317">[299]</a></sup> The prisoners killed 11 German <a href="/wiki/SS" class="mw-redirect" title="SS">SS</a> officers and a couple of Ukrainian camp guards, but the inmates were forced to run.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad1987337_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad1987337-318">[300]</a></sup> About 300 prisoners escaped, but 100 were recaptured and shot soon after escaping.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad1987341_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad1987341-319">[301]</a></sup> About 50 survived the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199898_317-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199898-317">[299]</a></sup> In October 1944, Jewish <i><a href="/wiki/Sonderkommando" title="Sonderkommando">Sonderkommandos</a></i> at Auschwitz attacked their guards and blew up Crematorium IV with explosives that had been smuggled in. Three German guards were killed during the uprising, one of whom was stuffed into an oven. The Sonderkommandos attempted a mass breakout, but all were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERees2005256.3D257_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERees2005256.3D257-320">[302]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Partisan_and_resistance_groups">Partisan and resistance groups</span></h4>
<p>While there were no independent Jewish resistance groups during the war, many joined other active partisan groups. Estimates of total Jewish participation in partisan units throughout Europe range from a low of 20,000 to a high of 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007780_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy2007780-321">[303]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the occupied Polish and Soviet territories, thousands of Jews fled into the swamps or forests and joined the partisans,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel1998100.E2.80.93101_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel1998100.E2.80.93101-322">[304]</a></sup> although the partisan movements did not always welcome them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016648_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016648-323">[305]</a></sup> An estimated 20,000 to 30,000 Jews joined the Soviet partisan movement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETec2001546_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETec2001546-324">[306]</a></sup> One of the famous Jewish partisan groups was the <a href="/wiki/Bielski_partisans" title="Bielski partisans">Bielski partisans</a> in Belarus, which was led by the Bielski brothers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel-325">[307]</a></sup> Some of the fighters in the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</a> of 1944 had participated in the Warsaw Ghetto Uprising of 1943. Jews also joined the Polish <a href="/wiki/Armia_Krajowa" class="mw-redirect" title="Armia Krajowa">Home Army</a> or other Polish forces. According to Timothy Snyder, "more Jews fought in the Warsaw Uprising of August 1944 than in the Warsaw Ghetto Uprising of April 1943".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010302_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010302-326">[308]</a></sup> Joining the partisans was an option only for the young and the fit who were willing to leave their families. Many Jewish families preferred to die together rather than be separated.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/French_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="French Jews">French Jews</a> were also highly active in the <a href="/wiki/French_Resistance" title="French Resistance">French Resistance</a>, with the percentage of Jews belonging to resistance groups being many times their percentage of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016273_327-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016273-327">[309]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">Zionist</a> Jews formed the <i><a href="/wiki/Armee_Juive" class="mw-redirect" title="Armee Juive">Armee Juive</a></i> (Jewish Army), which participated in armed resistance under a Zionist flag, smuggled Jews out of the country,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZuccotti1993274_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZuccotti1993274-328">[310]</a></sup> and participated in the liberation of Paris and other cities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZuccotti1993275_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZuccotti1993275-329">[311]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Jews_in_the_Allied_forces">Jews in the Allied forces</span></h4>
<p>As many as 1.5&#160;million Jewish soldiers fought in the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> armies, including 500,000 in the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>, 550,000 in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">U.S. Army</a>, 100,000 in the Polish army and 30,000 in the British army. About 200,000 Jewish soldiers serving in the Red Army died in the war, either in combat or murdered after being captured.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[312]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Brigade" title="Jewish Brigade">Jewish Brigade</a>, a unit of 5,000 Jewish volunteers from the <a href="/wiki/British_Mandate_of_Palestine" class="mw-redirect" title="British Mandate of Palestine">British Mandate of Palestine</a>, fought in the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaqueur2001351_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaqueur2001351-331">[313]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_experimentation">Medical experimentation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nazi_human_experimentation" title="Nazi human experimentation">Nazi human experimentation</a></div>
<p>The SS used the inmates of both the concentration and extermination camps as subjects of medical experiments. Both Jewish and non-Jewish prisoners were used for a variety of experiments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000229.E2.80.93230_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000229.E2.80.93230-332">[314]</a></sup> The most notorious of these physicians was <a href="/wiki/Josef_Mengele" title="Josef Mengele">Josef Mengele</a>, who worked in Auschwitz. His experiments included placing subjects in pressure chambers, testing drugs on them, freezing them, attempting to change their eye color by injecting chemicals into children's eyes, and amputations and other surgeries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarran2000384_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarran2000384-333">[315]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[s]</a></sup> Other experiments took place at <a href="/wiki/Buchenwald_concentration_camp" title="Buchenwald concentration camp">Buchenwald</a>, Dachau, <a href="/wiki/Natzweiler_concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Natzweiler concentration camp">Natzweiler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuengamme_concentration_camp" title="Neuengamme concentration camp">Neuengamme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ravensbr%C3%BCck_concentration_camp" title="Ravensbrück concentration camp">Ravensbrück</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_concentration_camp" title="Sachsenhausen concentration camp">Sachsenhausen</a>, and others. Some of the experiments dealt with sterilization of men and women, the treatment of war wounds, ways to counteract chemical weapons, research into new vaccines and drugs, and survival of harsh conditions. These experiments violated rules requiring consent for human experimentation and were conducted without regard to medical ethics. At least 7000, and likely more, prisoners were subjected to these experiments, and most died either during the experiments or afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFisher2001410.E2.80.93414_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFisher2001410.E2.80.93414-336">[317]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climax">Climax</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:May_1944_-_Jews_from_Carpathian_Ruthenia_arrive_at_Auschwitz-Birkenau.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/May_1944_-_Jews_from_Carpathian_Ruthenia_arrive_at_Auschwitz-Birkenau.jpg/220px-May_1944_-_Jews_from_Carpathian_Ruthenia_arrive_at_Auschwitz-Birkenau.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/May_1944_-_Jews_from_Carpathian_Ruthenia_arrive_at_Auschwitz-Birkenau.jpg/330px-May_1944_-_Jews_from_Carpathian_Ruthenia_arrive_at_Auschwitz-Birkenau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/May_1944_-_Jews_from_Carpathian_Ruthenia_arrive_at_Auschwitz-Birkenau.jpg/440px-May_1944_-_Jews_from_Carpathian_Ruthenia_arrive_at_Auschwitz-Birkenau.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="862" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:May_1944_-_Jews_from_Carpathian_Ruthenia_arrive_at_Auschwitz-Birkenau.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jews from <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Ruthenia" title="Carpathian Ruthenia">Carpathian Ruthenia</a> during arrival at Auschwitz, May 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most of the Jewish ghettos of <a href="/wiki/General_Government" title="General Government">General Government</a> were liquidated in 1942–1943, and their populations shipped to the camps for extermination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003256.E2.80.93257_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003256.E2.80.93257-337">[318]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010330.E2.80.93339.2C_375.E2.80.93379_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010330.E2.80.93339.2C_375.E2.80.93379-338">[319]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">[t]</a></sup> About 42,000 Jews were shot during the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Harvest_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Harvest Festival">Operation Harvest Festival</a> on 3–4 November 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[321]</a></sup> At the same time, rail shipments arrived regularly from western and southern Europe at the extermination camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010360.E2.80.93373.2C_386.E2.80.93389.2C_390.E2.80.93396_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010360.E2.80.93373.2C_386.E2.80.93389.2C_390.E2.80.93396-342">[322]</a></sup> Few Jews were shipped from the occupied Soviet territories to the camps: the killing of Jews in this zone was mostly left in the hands of the SS, aided by locally recruited auxiliaries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010345.E2.80.93353_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010345.E2.80.93353-343">[323]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">[u]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shipments of Jews to the camps had priority over anything but the army's needs on the German railways, and continued even in the face of the increasingly dire military situation at the end of 1942<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990376.E2.80.93378_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990376.E2.80.93378-346">[325]</a></sup> Army leaders and economic managers complained about this diversion of resources and at the killing of skilled Jewish workers;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKwiet200461.2C_69.E2.80.9371.2C_76.E2.80.9377_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKwiet200461.2C_69.E2.80.9371.2C_76.E2.80.9377-347">[326]</a></sup> however, Nazi leaders rated ideological imperatives above economic considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKwiet200477.E2.80.9378_348-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKwiet200477.E2.80.9378-348">[327]</a></sup> In fact, many of the war industries using slave labour were more productive when SS supervision was removed;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen200217_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen200217-349">[328]</a></sup> otherwise their brutality proved counterproductive.</p>
<p>By 1943, it was evident to the armed forces leadership that Germany was losing the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1998536.E2.80.93538_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1998536.E2.80.93538-350">[329]</a></sup> The scale of extermination slackened somewhat at the beginning of 1944 once the ghettos in occupied Poland were emptied,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016107.E2.80.93109_351-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016107.E2.80.93109-351">[330]</a></sup> but on 19 March 1944, Hitler ordered the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Margarethe" title="Operation Margarethe">military occupation of Hungary</a>, and dispatched Eichmann to Budapest to supervise the deportation of Hungarian Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans200295_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans200295-352">[331]</a></sup> More than 430,000 Hungarian Jews were shipped to Auschwitz after the occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016282.E2.80.93283_353-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016282.E2.80.93283-353">[332]</a></sup> During the deportations in May and June 1944,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2008343.E2.80.93348_354-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2008343.E2.80.93348-354">[333]</a></sup> up to 6,000 people were being gassed every day at Auschwitz.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">[334]</a></sup> During the Hungarian deportations, there were efforts to negotiate with the Allies to rescue Jews; at one point there was an attempt by Eichmann to exchange one million Jews for 10,000 trucks<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199876.E2.80.9377_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199876.E2.80.9377-356">[335]</a></sup>—the so-called "<a href="/wiki/Blood_for_goods" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood for goods">blood for goods</a>" proposal<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel201031_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel201031-357">[336]</a></sup> was made—but there was no real possibility of such a deal being struck on this scale.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199876.E2.80.9377_356-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199876.E2.80.9377-356">[335]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Escapes_and_early_Allied_responses">Escapes and early Allied responses</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Mass_Extermination_of_Jews_in_German_Occupied.pdf" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/The_Mass_Extermination_of_Jews_in_German_Occupied.pdf/page1-170px-The_Mass_Extermination_of_Jews_in_German_Occupied.pdf.jpg" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/The_Mass_Extermination_of_Jews_in_German_Occupied.pdf/page1-255px-The_Mass_Extermination_of_Jews_in_German_Occupied.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/The_Mass_Extermination_of_Jews_in_German_Occupied.pdf/page1-340px-The_Mass_Extermination_of_Jews_in_German_Occupied.pdf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="856" data-file-height="1281" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Mass_Extermination_of_Jews_in_German_Occupied.pdf" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"The Mass Extermination of Jews in German Occupied Poland", by the <a href="/wiki/Polish_government-in-exile" title="Polish government-in-exile">Polish government-in-exile</a> addressed to the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">wartime allies</a> of the then-<a href="/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations" title="Declaration by United Nations">United Nations</a>, 1942.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times#World_War_II" title="The New York Times">The New York Times §&#160;World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Karski" title="Jan Karski">Jan Karski</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polish_government-in-exile" title="Polish government-in-exile">Polish government-in-exile</a></div>
<p>Escapes from the camps were few, but not unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015532.E2.80.93533_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015532.E2.80.93533-358">[337]</a></sup> Some 928 prisoners attempted to escape from Auschwitz according to documents, including around 50 women. Among them were 150 Jews including four Jewish women. Only 196 escapes were confirmed as successful after the war ended, while 433 fugitives were recaptured by the SS. Another 254 prisoners who crossed the perimeter were never found.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[338]</a></sup> Assisting an escaping Jew in any way within occupied Poland was life-threatening due to decrees imposing mandatory death sentence for hiding them; later expanded to include the death penalty for any kind of aid to the Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaldiel1993184_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaldiel1993184-360">[339]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 1942, an escapee from Chełmno, <a href="/wiki/Szlama_Ber_Winer" title="Szlama Ber Winer">Szlama Ber Winer</a>, reached the Warsaw Ghetto, where he gave detailed information about the camp to the <a href="/wiki/Oyneg_Shabbos_(group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oyneg Shabbos (group)">Oneg Shabbat</a> group. His report, which became known by his pseudonym as the <a href="/wiki/Grojanowski_Report" title="Grojanowski Report">Grojanowski Report</a>, was smuggled out of the ghetto and reached London by June 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-yvChelmno_250-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yvChelmno-250">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[340]</a></sup> Also in 1942, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Karski" title="Jan Karski">Jan Karski</a> reported to the Allies on the plight of Jews in war-torn Poland,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrowe2008354_362-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrowe2008354-362">[341]</a></sup> after being smuggled into the Warsaw ghetto twice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000183_363-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000183-363">[342]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[v]</a></sup> In November and December 1942, the Polish government in-exile condemned the murder of Jews and called on the Allies to find ways to stop the extermination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELukas2012160_366-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELukas2012160-366">[344]</a></sup> This report and the Polish Government's lobbying efforts triggered the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Declaration_by_Members_of_the_United_Nations" title="Joint Declaration by Members of the United Nations">Joint Declaration by Members of the United Nations</a> of 17 December 1942 which made public and condemned the mass extermination of the Jews in German-occupied Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[345]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two Jews, <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Vrba" title="Rudolf Vrba">Rudolf Vrba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Wetzler" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfred Wetzler">Alfred Wetzler</a>, escaped from Auschwitz in April 1944, eventually reaching <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>. Their document about the mass murder at Auschwitz became known as the <a href="/wiki/Vrba-Wetzler_report" class="mw-redirect" title="Vrba-Wetzler report">Vrba-Wetzler report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKarny1998553.E2.80.93556_368-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKarny1998553.E2.80.93556-368">[346]</a></sup> The <i>New York Times</i> published material from the Vrba-Wetzler report in June and July 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-Brigham19440703_369-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brigham19440703-369">[347]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brigham19440706_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brigham19440706-370">[348]</a></sup> The subsequent pressure persuaded <a href="/wiki/Mikl%C3%B3s_Horthy" title="Miklós Horthy">Miklós Horthy</a> to bring the deportations of Hungarian Jews to Auschwitz to a halt on 9 July, saving up to 200,000 Jews from death.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">[349]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British and American governmental information offices feared publicising the information they had received. Although it was felt that the information was correct, the offices were concerned that the stories were so extreme that the public would discount them as exaggerations and thus undermine the credibility of both governments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENovick200023_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENovick200023-372">[350]</a></sup> The US government also hesitated to emphasise the atrocities against the Jews for fear of turning the war into a war about the Jews. Anti-Semitism and isolationism were common beliefs in the US prior to the US entry into the war, and the government wanted to avoid too great a focus on Jewish suffering in order to keep isolationism from gaining ground.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENovick200027.E2.80.9328_373-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENovick200027.E2.80.9328-373">[351]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_marches">Death marches</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_marches_(Holocaust)" title="Death marches (Holocaust)">Death marches (Holocaust)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pomnik_mogila_ofiar_marszu_smierci_Wodzislaw_Slaski.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Pomnik_mogila_ofiar_marszu_smierci_Wodzislaw_Slaski.JPG/220px-Pomnik_mogila_ofiar_marszu_smierci_Wodzislaw_Slaski.JPG" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Pomnik_mogila_ofiar_marszu_smierci_Wodzislaw_Slaski.JPG/330px-Pomnik_mogila_ofiar_marszu_smierci_Wodzislaw_Slaski.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Pomnik_mogila_ofiar_marszu_smierci_Wodzislaw_Slaski.JPG/440px-Pomnik_mogila_ofiar_marszu_smierci_Wodzislaw_Slaski.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1138" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pomnik_mogila_ofiar_marszu_smierci_Wodzislaw_Slaski.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Grave and Memorial in <a href="/wiki/Wodzis%C5%82aw" class="mw-redirect" title="Wodzisław">Wodzisław</a> of the most infamous Death march from <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz Birkenau</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wodzis%C5%82aw_%C5%9Al%C4%85ski" title="Wodzisław Śląski">Wodzisław Śląski</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By mid-1944, those Jewish communities within easy reach of the Nazi regime had been largely exterminated,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016107.E2.80.93109_351-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016107.E2.80.93109-351">[330]</a></sup> in proportions ranging from about 25 percent in France<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2001219_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2001219-374">[352]</a></sup> to more than 90 percent in Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPolonsky2001488_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPolonsky2001488-375">[353]</a></sup> On 5 May, Himmler claimed in a speech that "the Jewish question has in general been solved in Germany and in the countries occupied by Germany".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2012695_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2012695-376">[354]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the Soviet armed forces advanced, the camps in eastern Poland were closed down, with surviving inmates shipped to camps closer to Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016290.E2.80.93292_377-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016290.E2.80.93292-377">[355]</a></sup> Efforts were made to conceal evidence of what had happened in the camps and in the mass shootings. The gas chambers were dismantled, the crematoria dynamited, and the mass graves dug up and the corpses cremated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010410.E2.80.93412_378-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010410.E2.80.93412-378">[356]</a></sup> Local commanders continued to kill Jews, and to shuttle them from camp to camp by forced "death marches" until the last weeks of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-MapUSHMM_379-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MapUSHMM-379">[357]</a></sup></p>
<p>Already sick after months or years of violence and starvation, prisoners were forced to march out of the camps. Some were marched to train stations and then transported for days at a time without food or shelter in open freight cars and forced to march again at the other end to the new camp. Others were marched the entire distance to the new camp. Those who lagged behind or fell were shot. Around 250,000 Jews died during these marches.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder2007648.E2.80.93650_380-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder2007648.E2.80.93650-380">[358]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberation">Liberation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">Battle of Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Death of Adolf Hitler">Death of Adolf Hitler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague_Offensive" title="Prague Offensive">Prague Offensive</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">Victory in Europe Day</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eines_von_3_Massengr%C3%A4bern_in_Bergen-Belsen,_so_wie_es_von_den_Befreiern_vorgefunden_wurde,_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Eines_von_3_Massengr%C3%A4bern_in_Bergen-Belsen%2C_so_wie_es_von_den_Befreiern_vorgefunden_wurde%2C_1945.jpg/220px-Eines_von_3_Massengr%C3%A4bern_in_Bergen-Belsen%2C_so_wie_es_von_den_Befreiern_vorgefunden_wurde%2C_1945.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Eines_von_3_Massengr%C3%A4bern_in_Bergen-Belsen%2C_so_wie_es_von_den_Befreiern_vorgefunden_wurde%2C_1945.jpg/330px-Eines_von_3_Massengr%C3%A4bern_in_Bergen-Belsen%2C_so_wie_es_von_den_Befreiern_vorgefunden_wurde%2C_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Eines_von_3_Massengr%C3%A4bern_in_Bergen-Belsen%2C_so_wie_es_von_den_Befreiern_vorgefunden_wurde%2C_1945.jpg/440px-Eines_von_3_Massengr%C3%A4bern_in_Bergen-Belsen%2C_so_wie_es_von_den_Befreiern_vorgefunden_wurde%2C_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="418" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eines_von_3_Massengr%C3%A4bern_in_Bergen-Belsen,_so_wie_es_von_den_Befreiern_vorgefunden_wurde,_1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A grave inside Bergen-Belsen.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first major camp to be encountered by Allied troops, <a href="/wiki/Majdanek_concentration_camp" title="Majdanek concentration camp">Majdanek</a>, was discovered by the advancing Soviets on 25 July 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000165_381-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000165-381">[359]</a></sup> Treblinka, Sobibór, and Bełżec were never liberated, but were destroyed by the Germans in 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010411_382-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010411-382">[360]</a></sup> Auschwitz was liberated, also by the Soviets, on 27 January 1945;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitchcock2008283_383-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitchcock2008283-383">[361]</a></sup> Buchenwald by the Americans on 11 April;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitchcock2008297_384-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitchcock2008297-384">[362]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bergen-Belsen_concentration_camp" title="Bergen-Belsen concentration camp">Bergen-Belsen</a> was liberated by the British on 15 April;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitchcock2008340_385-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitchcock2008340-385">[363]</a></sup> Dachau was liberated by the Americans on 29 April;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1985798_386-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1985798-386">[364]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ravensbr%C3%BCck_concentration_camp" title="Ravensbrück concentration camp">Ravensbrück</a> was liberated by the Soviets on 30 April;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015577_387-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015577-387">[365]</a></sup> Mauthausen was liberated by the Americans on 5 May;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1985808.E2.80.93809_388-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1985808.E2.80.93809-388">[366]</a></sup> and the Red Cross took control of <a href="/wiki/Theresienstadt_concentration_camp" title="Theresienstadt concentration camp">Theresienstadt</a> on 4 May,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert1985810_389-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert1985810-389">[367]</a></sup> some days before the Soviets arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016762_390-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016762-390">[368]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Soviets found 7,600 inmates in Auschwitz.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitchcock2008289_391-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitchcock2008289-391">[369]</a></sup> Some 60,000 prisoners were discovered at Bergen-Belsen by the British <a href="/wiki/11th_Armoured_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="11th Armoured Division (United Kingdom)">11th Armoured Division</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11thUSHMM_392-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11thUSHMM-392">[370]</a></sup> 13,000 corpses lay unburied, and another 10,000 died from <a href="/wiki/Typhus" title="Typhus">typhus</a> or malnutrition over the following weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-BBUSHMM_393-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBUSHMM-393">[371]</a></sup></p>
<p>The BBC's <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dimbleby" title="Richard Dimbleby">Richard Dimbleby</a> described the scenes that greeted him and the British Army at Belsen:</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebensee_concentration_camp_prisoners_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Ebensee_concentration_camp_prisoners_1945.jpg/220px-Ebensee_concentration_camp_prisoners_1945.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Ebensee_concentration_camp_prisoners_1945.jpg/330px-Ebensee_concentration_camp_prisoners_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Ebensee_concentration_camp_prisoners_1945.jpg/440px-Ebensee_concentration_camp_prisoners_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2843" data-file-height="2087" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebensee_concentration_camp_prisoners_1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starving prisoners in Mauthausen camp liberated on 5 May 1945.</div>
</div>
</div>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Here over an acre of ground lay dead and dying people. You could not see which was which… The living lay with their heads against the corpses and around them moved the awful, ghostly procession of emaciated, aimless people, with nothing to do and with no hope of life, unable to move out of your way, unable to look at the terrible sights around them… Babies had been born here, tiny wizened things that could not live… A mother, driven mad, screamed at a British sentry to give her milk for her child, and thrust the tiny mite into his arms… He opened the bundle and found the baby had been dead for days. This day at Belsen was the most horrible of my life.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— Richard Dimbleby, 1945<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">[372]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Responses_to_the_Holocaust">Responses to the Holocaust</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_response_to_the_Holocaust" title="International response to the Holocaust">International response to the Holocaust</a></div>
<h3><span id="Perpetrator's_motivations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Perpetrator.27s_motivations">Perpetrator's motivations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_war_crimes" title="German war crimes">German war crimes</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_crimes_of_the_Wehrmacht" title="War crimes of the Wehrmacht">War crimes of the Wehrmacht</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Responsibility_for_the_Holocaust" title="Responsibility for the Holocaust">Responsibility for the Holocaust</a></div>
<p>In his 1965 essay "Command and Compliance", historian Hans Buchheim wrote there was no coercion to murder Jews and others, and all who committed such actions did so out of free will.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968372.E2.80.93373_395-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968372.E2.80.93373-395">[373]</a></sup> Buchheim wrote that the chances to avoid participating in killing Jews were available for perpetrators, although they did not often admit that after the war,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968372.E2.80.93373_395-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968372.E2.80.93373-395">[373]</a></sup> and that he found no evidence that SS men who refused to carry out criminal orders were sent to concentration camps or executed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968381_396-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968381-396">[374]</a></sup> Moreover, <i>SS</i> rules prohibited acts of gratuitous sadism and acts of sadism were taken on the individual initiative of those who were either especially cruel or who wished to prove themselves ardent Nazis.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968372.E2.80.93373_395-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968372.E2.80.93373-395">[373]</a></sup> Finally, he argued that those who committed crimes did so because they wished to conform to the values of the group and were afraid of being branded "weak" by their colleagues.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968386.E2.80.93387_397-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuchheim1968386.E2.80.93387-397">[375]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his 1992 monograph <i>Ordinary Men</i>, the historian <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Browning" title="Christopher Browning">Christopher Browning</a> examined the deeds of German <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Police_Battalion_101" title="Reserve Police Battalion 101">Reserve Police Battalion 101</a>, used for massacres and round-ups of Jews as well as deportations to the death camps. The members of the battalion were middle-aged men of working-class background who were too old for regular military duty.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning199844.E2.80.9348_398-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning199844.E2.80.9348-398">[376]</a></sup> They were given no special training for genocide and at first,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning1998183.E2.80.93184_399-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning1998183.E2.80.93184-399">[377]</a></sup> the commander gave his men the choice of opting out of direct participation in the killing of Jews if they found it too unpleasant. The majority chose not to opt out; fewer than 12 men, out of a battalion of 500 did so on the first occasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning199857_400-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning199857-400">[378]</a></sup> Browning argued that the men of the battalion killed out of peer pressure, not blood-lust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning1998171.E2.80.93189_401-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning1998171.E2.80.93189-401">[379]</a></sup></p>
<p>Historian Sergei Kudryashov studied the guards trained at the <a href="/wiki/Trawniki_concentration_camp#Key_role_of_Trawniki_men_in_the_Final_Solution" title="Trawniki concentration camp">Trawniki SS camp division</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Trawniki_men" title="Trawniki men">Trawniki men</a>" or "Trawniki guards"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004227_402-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004227-402">[380]</a></sup> who provided personnel for the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Reinhard" title="Operation Reinhard">Operation Reinhard</a> death camps and other concentration camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004230_403-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004230-403">[381]</a></sup> Most of them were former Red Army soldiers who volunteered to join the <i>SS</i> in order to get out of the POW camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004232.E2.80.93233_404-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004232.E2.80.93233-404">[382]</a></sup> The vast majority carried out the SS's expectations of how to treat Jews,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004234_405-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004234-405">[383]</a></sup> and most personally killed Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004234.E2.80.93235_406-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004234.E2.80.93235-406">[384]</a></sup> Agreeing with Browning, Kudryashov argued that the Trawniki men were examples of ordinary people becoming willing killers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004226_407-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKudryashov2004226-407">[385]</a></sup></p>
<p>Germans usually justified the <i>Einsatzgruppen'</i>s massacres on the grounds of anti-Bolshevik, anti-partisan or anti-bandit operations, but the historian <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Hillgruber" title="Andreas Hillgruber">Andreas Hillgruber</a> aruges that this was merely an excuse for the German Army's considerable involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_in_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust in Russia">Holocaust in Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHillgruber1989pp._102.E2.80.933_.28Yad_Yashem_p._121-3.29._408-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHillgruber1989pp._102.E2.80.933_.28Yad_Yashem_p._121-3.29.-408">[386]</a></sup> Hillgruber maintained that those German generals who claimed that the <i>Einsatzgruppen</i> were a necessary anti-partisan response were lying.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHillgruber1989pp._102.E2.80.933_.28Yad_Yashem_p._121-3.29._408-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHillgruber1989pp._102.E2.80.933_.28Yad_Yashem_p._121-3.29.-408">[386]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_F%C3%B6rster" title="Jürgen Förster">Jürgen Förster</a> agrees, and argued that the <i>Wehrmacht</i> played a key role in the Holocaust. He said it is wrong to describe the Holocaust as solely the work of the SS with the <i>Wehrmacht</i> as a passive and disapproving bystander.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEF.C3.B6rster1998280_409-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF.C3.B6rster1998280-409">[387]</a></sup></p>
<p>Army co-operation with the SS in anti-Bolshevik, anti-partisan and anti-Jewish operations was close and intensive. After a 1941 SS "anti-partisan" operation which killed over 14,000 Jews and only 1000 partisans, General <a href="/wiki/Max_von_Schenckendorff" title="Max von Schenckendorff">Max von Schenckendorff</a>, who commanded the <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_Center_Rear_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Army Group Center Rear Area">Army Group Center Rear Area</a>, ordered that all <i>Wehrmacht</i> <a href="/wiki/Security_Division_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Security Division (Germany)">security divisions</a> should emulate this example when on anti-partisan duty, and organized a joint SS-<i>Wehrmacht</i> seminar on how best to kill Jews. The event, that became known as the <a href="/wiki/Mogilev_Conference" title="Mogilev Conference">Mogilev Conference</a>, ended with a German unit killing Jews as a demonstration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEF.C3.B6rster1998276-277_410-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF.C3.B6rster1998276-277-410">[388]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="German_public">German public</span></h3>
<p>In his 1983 book, <i>Popular Opinion and Political Dissent in the Third Reich</i>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kershaw" title="Ian Kershaw">Ian Kershaw</a> examined everyday life in Bavaria during the Nazi period. Kershaw argued that the most common viewpoint of Bavarians was indifference towards the persecution of Jews. Kershaw argued that most Bavarians were vaguely aware of the genocide, but were vastly more concerned about the war than the "Final Solution".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrus198789.E2.80.9390_411-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrus198789.E2.80.9390-411">[389]</a></sup> Kershaw made the analogy that "the road to Auschwitz was built by hate, but paved with indifference".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans198971_412-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans198971-412">[390]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrus198791_413-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrus198791-413">[391]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kershaw's assessment that most Bavarians, and by implication most Germans, were indifferent to the Holocaust faced criticism from historians Otto Dov Kulka and Michael Kater. Kater maintained that Kershaw downplayed the extent of popular antisemitism, and that though admitting that most of the "spontaneous" antisemitic actions of Nazi Germany were staged, argued that because these actions involved substantial numbers of Germans, it is wrong to see the extreme antisemitism of the Nazis as coming solely from above.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrus198792_414-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrus198792-414">[392]</a></sup> Kulka argued that most Germans were more antisemitic than Kershaw portrayed them and that rather than "indifference", "passive complicity" would be a better term to describe the reaction of the German people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrus198793_415-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrus198793-415">[393]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a study focusing only on the views about Jews among Germans opposed to the Nazi regime, historian Christof Dipper in his 1983 essay "<i>Der Deutsche Widerstand und die Juden</i>" argued that the majority of the anti-Nazi national-conservatives were antisemitic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrus198792_414-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrus198792-414">[392]</a></sup> Though Dipper noted no one in the <a href="/wiki/German_resistance" class="mw-redirect" title="German resistance">German resistance</a> supported the Holocaust, he also commented that the national-conservatives did not intend to restore civil rights to the Jews after the planned overthrow of Hitler.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrus198792_414-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrus198792-414">[392]</a></sup></p>
<p>Research by the United States Holocaust Museum has established that because the camps were so widespread<sup id="cite_ref-416" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-416">[w]</a></sup> it is unlikely that the German population could avoid knowing about the persecutions and killings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELichtblau2013_173-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELichtblau2013-173">[164]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gellately" title="Robert Gellately">Robert Gellately</a> has argued that the German civilian population were, by and large, aware of what was happening. According to Gellately, the government openly announced the conspiracy through the media and civilians were aware of its every aspect except for the use of gas chambers.<sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-417">[394]</a></sup></p>

<p>The number of victims depends on which definition of the Holocaust is used.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045-10">[7]</a></sup> The number of Jewish victims is somewhere over 5 million,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045-10">[7]</a></sup> with upper estimates ranging from 5.9 million,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199887_429-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199887-429">[405]</a></sup> to 6 million,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001285_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001285-94">[87]</a></sup> or even over 6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002454_430-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2002454-430">[406]</a></sup> The broadest definition of the Holocaust would raise the death toll to 17&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045-10">[7]</a></sup> A research project conducted by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum" title="United States Holocaust Memorial Museum">United States Holocaust Memorial Museum</a> estimated that 15 to 20 million people died or were imprisoned during the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELichtblau2013_173-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELichtblau2013-173">[164]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_Rummel" title="Rudolph Rummel">Rudolph Rummel</a> estimates the total <a href="/wiki/Democide" title="Democide">democidal</a> death toll of Nazi Germany to be 21 million.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jewish_death_toll">Jewish death toll</span></h3>
