<p>Adolf Eichmann, one of the principal architects of the Holocaust, gave a figure of 6 million Jewish victims.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901797_432-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901797-432">[408]</a></sup> This number was also used in July 1945 by <a href="/wiki/Abba_Kovner" title="Abba Kovner">Abba Kovner</a> and then later by the first post-war trials of perpetrators.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMichman2012197.E2.80.93198_433-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichman2012197.E2.80.93198-433">[409]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Yad_Vashem" title="Yad Vashem">Yad Vashem</a> Museum writes: "There is no precise figure for the number of Jews killed in the Holocaust. ... All the serious research confirms that the number of victims was between five and six million."<sup id="cite_ref-YadVashemnumbers_434-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YadVashemnumbers-434">[410]</a></sup> Yad Vashem has been able to find documentation of more than three million names of Jewish victims killed.<sup id="cite_ref-435" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-435">[411]</a></sup></p>
<p>The early postwar calculations ranged from about 4.2 to 4.5&#160;million by <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Reitlinger" title="Gerald Reitlinger">Gerald Reitlinger</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMichman2012197_436-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichman2012197-436">[412]</a></sup> and 5.1&#160;million from <a href="/wiki/Raul_Hilberg" title="Raul Hilberg">Raul Hilberg</a>, to 5.95&#160;million from <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Lestschinsky" title="Jacob Lestschinsky">Jacob Lestschinsky</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901797_432-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901797-432">[408]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yehuda_Bauer" title="Yehuda Bauer">Yehuda Bauer</a> and Robert Rozett in the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_of_the_Holocaust" title="Encyclopedia of the Holocaust">Encyclopedia of the Holocaust</a></i> estimate 5.59–5.86&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799_437-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799-437">[413]</a></sup> A study led by <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Benz" title="Wolfgang Benz">Wolfgang Benz</a> suggests 5.29 to 6.20&#160;million. These estimates derive from comparing census records from before and after the war as well as the surviving German documentation on deportations and killings.<sup id="cite_ref-YadVashemnumbers_434-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YadVashemnumbers-434">[410]</a></sup> Martin Gilbert arrived at a "minimum estimate" of over 5.75&#160;million Jewish victims.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001245_438-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001245-438">[414]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Dawidowicz" title="Lucy Dawidowicz">Lucy S. Dawidowicz</a> used the pre-war census figures to estimate that 5.934&#160;million Jews died.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDawidowicz1986403_418-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDawidowicz1986403-418">[395]</a></sup></p>
<p>The roughly six million killed in the Holocaust represent one third of the entire world population of Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001291_302-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2001291-302">[287]</a></sup> The victims were about two-thirds of European Jewry, based on an estimated number of about 9.7 million Jews in Europe at the start of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel199887_429-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel199887-429">[405]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett1799_439-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett1799-439">[415]</a></sup> Of those victims, 1.5 million were children.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeren2001115_440-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeren2001115-440">[416]</a></sup> Much of the uncertainty around how many Jews died comes from the lack of a reliable figure for the number of Jews in Europe in 1939, the numerous border changes that make avoiding double-counting of victims difficult, the lack of accurate records from the perpetrators, and uncertainty about when exactly the end date should be and whether deaths occurring months after the liberation but caused by the persecution should be counted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMichman2012197_436-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichman2012197-436">[412]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_camps">Death camps</span></h4>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz-Birkenau</a> over 1,000,000 people were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-MMABvictims_441-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MMABvictims-441">[417]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiper1998a62_442-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiper1998a62-442">[418]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Treblinka_extermination_camp" title="Treblinka extermination camp">Treblinka</a> 870,000<sup id="cite_ref-yvTreb_272-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yvTreb-272">[257]</a></sup> to 925,000 Jews were murdered.<sup id="cite_ref-443" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-443">[419]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%82%C5%BCec_extermination_camp" title="Bełżec extermination camp">Bełżec</a>, between 434,000<sup id="cite_ref-444" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-444">[420]</a></sup> and 600,000 Jews were slaughtered.<sup id="cite_ref-yvBelzec_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yvBelzec-267">[252]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Che%C5%82mno_extermination_camp" title="Chełmno extermination camp">Chełmno</a>, between 152,000<sup id="cite_ref-445" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-445">[421]</a></sup> and 320,000 Jews were executed.<sup id="cite_ref-yvChelmno_250-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yvChelmno-250">[238]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Sobib%C3%B3r_extermination_camp" title="Sobibór extermination camp">Sobibór</a>, between 170,000<sup id="cite_ref-446" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-446">[422]</a></sup> and 250,000 Jews were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-yvSob_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yvSob-271">[256]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Majdanek_concentration_camp" title="Majdanek concentration camp">Majdanek</a>, depending on the various sources, between 79,000 and 235,000 Jews were murdered.<sup id="cite_ref-yvMaj_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yvMaj-269">[254]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reszka2005_447-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reszka2005-447">[423]</a></sup> For the death camps, 80–90% of the victims are estimated to be Jews. They accounted for half the total number of Jews killed in the entire Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDawidowicz1986403_418-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDawidowicz1986403-418">[395]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Jewish_deaths">Other Jewish deaths</span></h4>
<p>Around one million Jews were killed by the <i>Einsatzgruppen</i> in the occupied Soviet territories,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000221.E2.80.93222_448-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000221.E2.80.93222-448">[424]</a></sup> an approximate figure, since the <i>Einsatzgruppen</i> reports did not always survive the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERhodes2002274_449-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERhodes2002274-449">[425]</a></sup> Many more died through execution or of disease and malnutrition in the ghettos of Poland before they could be deported.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201629.E2.80.9331_450-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201629.E2.80.9331-450">[426]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="By_country">By country</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_285_Bild-04413,_KZ_Auschwitz,_Einfahrt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Bundesarchiv_B_285_Bild-04413%2C_KZ_Auschwitz%2C_Einfahrt.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_B_285_Bild-04413%2C_KZ_Auschwitz%2C_Einfahrt.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Bundesarchiv_B_285_Bild-04413%2C_KZ_Auschwitz%2C_Einfahrt.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_B_285_Bild-04413%2C_KZ_Auschwitz%2C_Einfahrt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Bundesarchiv_B_285_Bild-04413%2C_KZ_Auschwitz%2C_Einfahrt.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_B_285_Bild-04413%2C_KZ_Auschwitz%2C_Einfahrt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="504" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_285_Bild-04413,_KZ_Auschwitz,_Einfahrt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
'Death Gate' to Auschwitz-Birkenau, 1945 photo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Of Poland's 3.3&#160;million Jews, about 90 percent were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPolonsky2001488_375-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPolonsky2001488-375">[353]</a></sup> At the beginning of World War II, the Jewish population of the Baltic States was around 350,000 in total: 250,000 in Lithuania, 95,000 in Latvia, and 4,500 in Estonia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaqueu200151.E2.80.9352_451-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaqueu200151.E2.80.9352-451">[427]</a></sup> By the end of 1941, close to 230,000 Jews in Latvia and Lithuania had been murdered during the previous six months.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert199356_452-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert199356-452">[428]</a></sup> Of 4,000 Jews in Estonia before the German invasion, some 3,000 fled to the Soviet Union. The remaining 1,000 were all murdered by the SS killing squads.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert199349_453-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert199349-453">[429]</a></sup> Finland had about 2000 Jews prior to the outbreak of war, but lost only 7 in the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup></p>
<p>Soviet figures are problematic because of the uncertainty of how many refugees were in the areas of the Soviet Union occupied by the Germans. There were 3,020,000 Jews living in the Soviet Union in 1939 and the losses were between 1 and 1.1 million. Almost all Jews within the areas occupied by the Germans were killed during the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_Encyclopedia" title="Holocaust Encyclopedia">Holocaust Encyclopedia</a>, there were 523,000 Jews in Germany in 1933. Following the Nazi takeover, many left the country. About 202,000 Jews remained in Germany and 57,000 in Austria after the invasion of Poland. The majority died in the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-HEn1_455-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEn1-455">[431]</a></sup> The Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia had about 118,000 prior to deportations beginning, and 78,150 died during the Holocaust. Slovakia had almost 89,000 Jews at the start of 1942 with losses of between 68,000 and 71,000, with an unknown number of refugees in transit who were caught and died in Slovakia. The exact number of pre-war Hungarian Jews is complicated by the changes in borders during the war as well as no precise figures on those Jews who were considered Jews only by racial definitions. Rough estimates give 825,000 Jews in Hungary during the war, with losses ranging from 550,000 to 569,000. Italy had about 44,500 Jews and 7680 were killed in the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Western Europe, Belgium lost 28,900 of a pre-war population of 65,700 Jews. There were approximately 7800 Jews in Denmark before the Holocaust,<sup id="cite_ref-456" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-456">[y]</a></sup> most of whom survived the war. France had approximately 350,000 Jews at the start of deportations,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup> and between 73,500<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009123_457-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009123-457">[432]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-458" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-458">[z]</a></sup> and 77,300 died in the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-459" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-459">[aa]</a></sup> Luxembourg had about 3500 Jews before the occupation and about 1950 died. About 100,000 of 140,000 Dutch Jews perished in the Holocaust. Norway had 1700 Jews and lost 762.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Balkans, Bulgaria deported none of its Jewish citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-461" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-461">[ab]</a></sup> Greece had about 77,000 Jews prior to the German and Italian invasion, and 60,000 to 67,000 of them died. Romania's changes of borders make it difficult to give precise figures, but the pre-war population of Jews was around 610,000. Between 271,000 and 287,000 lost their lives in the Holocaust,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup> but most of the victims were not from the heartland of Romania but from regions under Romanian control during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009114_462-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009114-462">[434]</a></sup> Yugoslavia had about 78,000 Jews prior to the war, and lost between 56,000 and 67,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-Jewish">Non-Jewish</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavs">Slavs</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Generalplan Ost</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hunger_Plan" title="Hunger Plan">Hunger Plan</a></div>
<p>The Nazis considered the Slavs as subhumans,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008174.E2.80.93175_463-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008174.E2.80.93175-463">[435]</a></sup> or <i><a href="/wiki/Untermenschen" class="mw-redirect" title="Untermenschen">Untermenschen</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder1976359_464-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder1976359-464">[436]</a></sup> Heinrich Himmler in a secret memorandum dated 25 May 1940 expressed his own thoughts and the future plans for the populations in the East.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritz201123_465-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritz201123-465">[437]</a></sup> Himmler stated that it was in the German interests to foster divisions between the ethnic groups in the East. He also wanted to restrict non-Germans in the conquered territories to schools which would only teach them how to write their own name, count up to 500 and to obey Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2012450.E2.80.93452_466-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2012450.E2.80.93452-466">[438]</a></sup></p>
<p>Himmler's General Plan East, or <i><a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Generalplan Ost</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritz201193_467-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritz201193-467">[439]</a></sup> which was agreed to by Hitler in the summer of 1942,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMazower2008204-205_468-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMazower2008204-205-468">[440]</a></sup> involved exterminating, expelling, or enslaving most or all <a href="/wiki/Slav" class="mw-redirect" title="Slav">Slavs</a> from their lands so as to make <a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">living space</a> for German settlers, something that would be carried out over a period of 20–30 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMazower2008208.E2.80.93211_469-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMazower2008208.E2.80.93211-469">[441]</a></sup> Though Generalplan Ost was never fully implemented,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritz2011p317_470-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritz2011p317-470">[442]</a></sup> historian <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_Rummel" title="Rudolph Rummel">Rudolph Rummel</a> estimates the number of Slav civilians and POWs murdered by the Germans to be 10,547,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Rummel1992_471-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rummel1992-471">[443]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_Poles">Ethnic Poles</span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation" title="Nazi crimes against the Polish nation">Nazi crimes against the Polish nation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Poland_(1939%E2%80%9345)" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of Poland (1939–45)">Occupation of Poland (1939–45)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacification_actions_in_German-occupied_Poland" title="Pacification actions in German-occupied Poland">Pacification actions in German-occupied Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Special_Prosecution_Book-Poland" title="Special Prosecution Book-Poland">Special Prosecution Book-Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Poland" title="The Holocaust in Poland">The Holocaust in Poland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg/220px-Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg/330px-Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/66/Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="336" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Polish civilians executed in Warsaw.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>German planners in November 1939 called for "the complete destruction" of all <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGellately2001153_472-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGellately2001153-472">[444]</a></sup> Poland under German occupation was to be cleared of Poles and settled by German colonists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerghahn199932.E2.80.9333_473-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerghahn199932.E2.80.9333-473">[445]</a></sup> The Polish political leadership and other leaders were the targets of an organized campaign of murder.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009112_474-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009112-474">[446]</a></sup> But German planners decided against a genocide of ethnic Poles on the same scale as against Jews, at least in the short term.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGellately2001154_475-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGellately2001154-475">[447]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Execution_of_Poles_by_German_Einsatzkommando_Oktober_1939.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Execution_of_Poles_by_German_Einsatzkommando_Oktober_1939.jpg/220px-Execution_of_Poles_by_German_Einsatzkommando_Oktober_1939.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Execution_of_Poles_by_German_Einsatzkommando_Oktober_1939.jpg/330px-Execution_of_Poles_by_German_Einsatzkommando_Oktober_1939.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Execution_of_Poles_by_German_Einsatzkommando_Oktober_1939.jpg/440px-Execution_of_Poles_by_German_Einsatzkommando_Oktober_1939.jpg 2x" data-file-width="743" data-file-height="471" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Execution_of_Poles_by_German_Einsatzkommando_Oktober_1939.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Execution of Poles by <i><a href="/wiki/Einsatzkommando" title="Einsatzkommando">Einsatzkommando</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Leszno" title="Leszno">Leszno</a>, October 1939.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 1.8 and 1.9&#160;million non-Jewish Polish citizens perished at German hands during the course of the war, about four-fifths of whom were ethnic <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> with the rest ethnic Ukrainians and Belarusians.<sup id="cite_ref-PolishVictims_420-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PolishVictims-420">[397]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PiotrowskiPIP_421-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PiotrowskiPIP-421">[398]</a></sup> At least 200,000 of these victims died in concentration camps with about 146,000 being killed in Auschwitz. Many others died as a result of general massacres or uprisings such as the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</a> where between 120,000 and 200,000 civilians were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiotrowski1998295_476-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiotrowski1998295-476">[448]</a></sup></p>
<p>The policy of the Germans in Poland included reducing food rations, deliberate lowering of public hygiene, and the deprivation of medical services. The general mortality rate rose from 13 to 18 per thousand.<sup id="cite_ref-477" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-477">[449]</a></sup> Overall, about 5.6&#160;million of the victims of World War II were Polish citizens,<sup id="cite_ref-PiotrowskiPIP_421-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PiotrowskiPIP-421">[398]</a></sup> both Jewish and non-Jewish, and over the course of the war Poland lost 16 percent of its pre-war population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiotrowski1998305_478-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiotrowski1998305-478">[450]</a></sup> Over 90 percent of the death toll came through non-military losses, through various deliberate actions by Germany and the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiotrowski1998295_476-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiotrowski1998295-476">[448]</a></sup> Polish children were also kidnapped by the Germans in order to be "Germanized", with perhaps as many as 200,000 children being stolen from their families for this purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELukas201225.E2.80.9327_479-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELukas201225.E2.80.9327-479">[451]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_West_Slavs">Other West Slavs</span></h5>
<p>Other West Slavic populations were persecuted. About 350,000 <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovak</a> citizens died as a result of German actions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELatawski2001216.E2.80.93217_480-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELatawski2001216.E2.80.93217-480">[452]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_Serbs_and_other_South_Slavs">Ethnic Serbs and other South Slavs</span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_persecution_of_Serbs" title="World War II persecution of Serbs">World War II persecution of Serbs</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Usta%C5%A1e_sawing_off_the_head_of_a_Serb_civilian.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Usta%C5%A1e_sawing_off_the_head_of_a_Serb_civilian.jpg/170px-Usta%C5%A1e_sawing_off_the_head_of_a_Serb_civilian.jpg" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Usta%C5%A1e_sawing_off_the_head_of_a_Serb_civilian.jpg/255px-Usta%C5%A1e_sawing_off_the_head_of_a_Serb_civilian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Usta%C5%A1e_sawing_off_the_head_of_a_Serb_civilian.jpg/340px-Usta%C5%A1e_sawing_off_the_head_of_a_Serb_civilian.jpg 2x" data-file-width="408" data-file-height="569" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Usta%C5%A1e_sawing_off_the_head_of_a_Serb_civilian.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Croatian Ustaše sawing off the head of Branko Jungić, an ethnic <a href="/wiki/Serb" class="mw-redirect" title="Serb">Serb</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_(region)" title="Bosnia (region)">Bosnia</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Germans had specific orders from Hitler to fight ruthlessly against the Serbs, who, besides being potential allies of the Russians, were considered <i><a href="/wiki/Untermenschen" class="mw-redirect" title="Untermenschen">Untermenschen</a></i> (sub-humans).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomasevich2001744_481-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomasevich2001744-481">[453]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e" title="Ustaše">Ustaše</a> collaborators conducted a systematic extermination of large numbers of people for political, religious or racial reasons. The most numerous victims were <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a> and others were also victims.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMojzes201154.E2.80.9355_482-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMojzes201154.E2.80.9355-482">[454]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum" title="United States Holocaust Memorial Museum">United States Holocaust Memorial Museum</a> reports that between 77,000 and 99,000 persons were killed at the <a href="/wiki/Jasenovac_concentration_camp" title="Jasenovac concentration camp">Jasenovac concentration camp</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-483" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-483">[455]</a></sup> with estimates ranging from a low of 20,000 to as many as a million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMojzes201155-56_484-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMojzes201155-56-484">[456]</a></sup> Yad Vashem reports that over 500,000 Serbs were murdered by the Ustaše,<sup id="cite_ref-485" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-485">[457]</a></sup> with other estimates being lower at around 330,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009119_486-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009119-486">[458]</a></sup> Other, Serbian, estimates range from 600,000 to 1 million Serbian deaths during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMojzes201155.E2.80.9356_487-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMojzes201155.E2.80.9356-487">[459]</a></sup> Excluding Slovenes under Italian rule, about 55,000 civilian <a href="/wiki/Slovenes" title="Slovenes">Slovenes</a> were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMojzes201173_488-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMojzes201173-488">[460]</a></sup> Estimates of Bosnian Muslims killed during the war range from 75,000<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMojzes201173.E2.80.9374_489-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMojzes201173.E2.80.9374-489">[461]</a></sup> to 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMojzes201198_490-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMojzes201198-490">[462]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanian</a> collaborationists cooperated with the Germans in an extensive persecution of non-Albanians. The Albanian <a href="/wiki/21st_Waffen_Mountain_Division_of_the_SS_Skanderbeg" title="21st Waffen Mountain Division of the SS Skanderbeg">SS Skenderbeg Division</a> participated in rounding up Jews as well as the killing and looting of Serbian areas. 3,000 to 10,000 Kosovo Serbs were murdered by the Albanians during the war, and another 30,000 to 100,000 were expelled.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMojzes201194.E2.80.9395_491-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMojzes201194.E2.80.9395-491">[463]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Slavs">East Slavs</span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Byelorussia_during_World_War_II" title="German occupation of Byelorussia during World War II">German occupation of Byelorussia during World War II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reichskommissariat_Ukraine" title="Reichskommissariat Ukraine">Reichskommissariat Ukraine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1970-043-52,_Russland,_bei_Minsk,_tote_Zivilisten.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1970-043-52%2C_Russland%2C_bei_Minsk%2C_tote_Zivilisten.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1970-043-52%2C_Russland%2C_bei_Minsk%2C_tote_Zivilisten.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1970-043-52%2C_Russland%2C_bei_Minsk%2C_tote_Zivilisten.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1970-043-52%2C_Russland%2C_bei_Minsk%2C_tote_Zivilisten.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1970-043-52%2C_Russland%2C_bei_Minsk%2C_tote_Zivilisten.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1970-043-52%2C_Russland%2C_bei_Minsk%2C_tote_Zivilisten.jpg 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="530" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1970-043-52,_Russland,_bei_Minsk,_tote_Zivilisten.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mass murder of Soviet civilians near <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, Belarus, 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Soviet civilian populations in the occupied areas were also heavily persecuted outside of events taking place in the frontline warfare of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016186.E2.80.93192_492-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016186.E2.80.93192-492">[464]</a></sup> Villages throughout the Soviet Union were destroyed by German troops.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritz2011333.E2.80.93334_493-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritz2011333.E2.80.93334-493">[465]</a></sup> Germans rounded up civilians for forced labour in Germany as well as causing famines by taking foodstuffs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016214.E2.80.93215_494-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016214.E2.80.93215-494">[466]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1995 The Russian Academy of Sciences reported that <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="World War II casualties of the Soviet Union">the number of civilian victims in the USSR</a> who were murdered at German hands, including Jews, totaled 13.7&#160;million dead, 20% of the 68 million persons in the occupied USSR. This included 7.4&#160;million victims of German genocide and reprisals.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_495-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-495">[467]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Belarus, Germany imposed a regime in the country that deported some 380,000 people for slave labour and killed hundreds of thousands of civilians. More than 600 villages had their entire populations killed and at least 5,295 Belarusian settlements were destroyed by the Germans. According to Timothy Snyder, of "the nine million people who were on the territory of Soviet Belarus in 1941, some 1.6 million were killed by the Germans in actions away from battlefields, including about 700,000 prisoners of war, 500,000 Jews, and 320,000 people counted as partisans (the vast majority of whom were unarmed civilians)".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010250.E2.80.93251_496-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010250.E2.80.93251-496">[468]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_POWs">Soviet POWs</span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208,_KZ_Mauthausen,_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208%2C_KZ_Mauthausen%2C_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg 2x" data-file-width="779" data-file-height="494" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_192-208,_KZ_Mauthausen,_Sowjetische_Kriegsgefangene.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Naked Soviet POWs in Mauthausen concentration camp. Unknown date.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The United States Holocaust Memorial Museum has estimated that 3.3 million of the 5.7 million Soviet POWs died in German custody.<sup id="cite_ref-497" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-497">[469]</a></sup> The death rates decreased as the POWs were needed to work as slaves to help the German war effort; by 1943, half a million of them had been deployed as <a href="/wiki/Slave_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave labour">slave labour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006125_419-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006125-419">[396]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Romani_people">Romani people</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Porajmos</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Antiziganism" class="mw-redirect" title="Antiziganism">Antiziganism</a></div>
<p>The Romani were subject to discrimination under the Nuremberg racial laws.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich201050_498-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich201050-498">[470]</a></sup> The Germans saw the Romani as hereditary criminals and "asocials" and this was reflected in their classification in the concentration camps where they were usually counted among the asocials and given black triangles to wear.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2015378.E2.80.93379_499-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2015378.E2.80.93379-499">[471]</a></sup> Because the <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a> are traditionally private with a culture based on <a href="/wiki/Oral_history" title="Oral history">oral history</a>, less is known about their experience than is known about any other group.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200047_500-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200047-500">[472]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yehuda_Bauer" title="Yehuda Bauer">Yehuda Bauer</a> writes that the lack of information can be attributed to the Romani's distrust and suspicion, and to their humiliation, because some of the <a href="/wiki/Taboo" title="Taboo">taboos</a> in Romani culture regarding hygiene and sex were violated at Auschwitz.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer1998453_501-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer1998453-501">[473]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Persecution_of_Roma.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Persecution_of_Roma.gif/330px-Persecution_of_Roma.gif" width="330" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Persecution_of_Roma.gif/495px-Persecution_of_Roma.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/96/Persecution_of_Roma.gif 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="420" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Persecution_of_Roma.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of persecution of the Roma</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The treatment of the Romani was not consistent across German-occupied territories, with those in France and the Low Countries subject to restrictions on movement and some confinement to collection camps. Those in Central and Eastern Europe were sent to concentration camps and murdered by soldiers and execution squads.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010418.E2.80.93421_502-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010418.E2.80.93421-502">[474]</a></sup> Before being sent to the camps, the victims were herded into ghettos, including several hundred into the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto" title="Warsaw Ghetto">Warsaw Ghetto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USHMMDepoWar_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USHMMDepoWar-210">[200]</a></sup> Further east, teams of <i>Einsatzgruppen</i> tracked down Romani encampments and murdered the inhabitants on the spot, leaving no records of the victims. They were also targeted by the allies of the Germans, such as the <a href="/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e" title="Ustaše">Ustaše</a> regime in <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, where a large number of Romani were killed in the Jasenovac concentration camp,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010418.E2.80.93421_502-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010418.E2.80.93421-502">[474]</a></sup> with the total killed in Croatia numbering about 28,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009119_486-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009119-486">[458]</a></sup> After the Germans occupied Hungary, a thousand Romani were deported to Auschwitz.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009114_462-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009114-462">[434]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 1942, the Romani were placed under similar labour and social laws to the Jews. On 16 December 1942, Heinrich Himmler issued a decree that "Gypsy Mischlinge [mixed breeds], Roma Gypsies, and members of the clans of Balkan origins who are not of German blood"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer1998444_503-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer1998444-503">[475]</a></sup> should be sent to Auschwitz, unless they had served in the <i><a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer1998444_503-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer1998444-503">[475]</a></sup> This was adjusted on 15 November 1943, when Himmler ordered that, in the occupied Soviet areas, "sedentary Gypsies and part-Gypsies are to be treated as citizens of the country. Nomadic Gypsies and part-Gypsies are to be placed on the same level as Jews and placed in concentration camps."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer1998445_504-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer1998445-504">[476]</a></sup> Bauer argues that this adjustment reflected Nazi ideology that the Romani, originally an Aryan population, had been "spoiled" by non-Romani blood.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer1998446_505-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer1998446-505">[477]</a></sup></p>
<p>Donald Niewyk and Frances Nicosia write that the death toll was at least 130,000 of the nearly one million Romani in German-occupied Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200047_500-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200047-500">[472]</a></sup> Michael Berenbaum writes that serious scholarly estimates lie between 90,000 and 220,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006126_506-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2006126-506">[478]</a></sup> The United States Holocaust Memorial Museum calculates a death toll of at least 220,000.<sup id="cite_ref-RomaUSHMM_422-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RomaUSHMM-422">[399]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ian_Hancock" title="Ian Hancock">Ian Hancock</a> has argued in favour of a much higher figure of between 500,000 and 1,500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock2004383.E2.80.9396_425-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock2004383.E2.80.9396-425">[401]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Persons_of_color">Persons of color</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_black_people_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Persecution of black people in Nazi Germany">Persecution of black people in Nazi Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhineland_Bastard" title="Rhineland Bastard">Rhineland Bastard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany#Other_.22non-Aryans.22" title="Racial policy of Nazi Germany">Racial policy of Nazi Germany §&#160;Other "non-Aryans"</a></div>
<p>The number of Afro-Germans in Germany when the Nazis came to power is variously estimated at 5,000–25,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELusane200397.E2.80.938_507-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELusane200397.E2.80.938-507">[479]</a></sup> It is not clear whether these figures included Asians. Although blacks in Germany and German-occupied Europe were subjected to incarceration, sterilization, murder, and other abuse, there was no programme to kill all of them as there was for the Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-508" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-508">[480]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aktion_brand.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Aktion_brand.jpg/170px-Aktion_brand.jpg" width="170" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Aktion_brand.jpg/255px-Aktion_brand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Aktion_brand.jpg/340px-Aktion_brand.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2218" data-file-height="3056" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aktion_brand.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hitler's order for Action T4.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Disabled_and_mentally_ill">Disabled and mentally ill</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Nazi_eugenics" title="Nazi eugenics">Nazi eugenics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aktion_T4" title="Aktion T4">Aktion T4</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erbkrank" title="Erbkrank">Erbkrank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_for_the_Prevention_of_Hereditarily_Diseased_Offspring" title="Law for the Prevention of Hereditarily Diseased Offspring">Law for the Prevention of Hereditarily Diseased Offspring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Life_unworthy_of_life" title="Life unworthy of life">Life unworthy of life</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Schloss_Hartheim" title="Schloss Hartheim">Schloss Hartheim</a></div>
<p>Nazis used the phrase <i>Lebensunwertes Leben</i> (<a href="/wiki/Life_unworthy_of_life" title="Life unworthy of life">Life unworthy of life</a>) in reference to their disabled or mentally-ill victims.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELifton200021_509-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELifton200021-509">[481]</a></sup> In July 1933, the <a href="/wiki/Law_for_the_Prevention_of_Hereditarily_Diseased_Offspring" title="Law for the Prevention of Hereditarily Diseased Offspring">Sterilization Law</a> allowing for compulsory sterilization of the "inferior" was passed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEProctor1988101.E2.80.93103_510-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProctor1988101.E2.80.93103-510">[482]</a></sup> In the first year of operation, this <a href="/wiki/Nazi_eugenics" title="Nazi eugenics">eugenics policy</a> had over 80,000 cases, which were decided in favour of sterilization over 90 percent of the time. Estimates for the total number of involuntary sterilizations during the whole of the Third Reich range from 300,000 to 400,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEProctor1988106.E2.80.93108_511-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProctor1988106.E2.80.93108-511">[483]</a></sup> In October 1939 <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> signed a "euthanasia decree" backdated to 1 September 1939 that authorized <i><a href="/wiki/Reichsleiter" title="Reichsleiter">Reichsleiter</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Bouhler" title="Philipp Bouhler">Philipp Bouhler</a>, the chief of <a href="/wiki/Hitler%27s_Chancellery" title="Hitler's Chancellery">Hitler's Chancellery</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Brandt" title="Karl Brandt">Karl Brandt</a>, Hitler's personal physician, to carry out the programme of involuntary euthanasia, known as <i>Action T4</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurleighWippermann1991142.E2.80.93149_512-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurleighWippermann1991142.E2.80.93149-512">[484]</a></sup> T4 was mainly directed at adults, but the euthanasia against children also began in October 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009171_513-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009171-513">[485]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Action T4</i> programme aimed to maintain the racial purity of the German people by killing or <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_sterilization#Germany" title="Compulsory sterilization">sterilizing</a> citizens who were judged to be <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">disabled</a> or suffering from <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">mental disorders</a>. The program was named after <a href="/wiki/Tiergartenstra%C3%9Fe" title="Tiergartenstraße">Tiergartenstraße</a> 4, the address of a villa in the Berlin borough of <a href="/wiki/Tiergarten,_Berlin" title="Tiergarten, Berlin">Tiergarten</a>, where the various organizations involved were headquartered.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000252.E2.80.93261_514-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000252.E2.80.93261-514">[486]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 1939 and 1941, 80,000 to 100,000 mentally-ill adults in institutions were killed; 5,000 children in institutions; and 1,000 Jews in institutions. There were also specialized killing centres, where the deaths are estimated as 20,000, according to Georg Renno, the deputy director of <a href="/wiki/Schloss_Hartheim" title="Schloss Hartheim">Schloss Hartheim</a>, one of the euthanasia centers, or 400,000, according to Frank Zeireis, the commandant of Mauthausen concentration camp.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELifton2000142_515-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELifton2000142-515">[487]</a></sup> Overall, the number of mentally and physically handicapped murdered was about 150,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200048_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200048-31">[26]</a></sup> Despite not being formally ordered to take part, <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">psychiatrists</a> and many psychiatric institutions took part in the planning and carrying out of the <i>Action T4</i> at every stage, and constituted the connection to the later annihilation of Jews and others in the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStrous2007_516-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStrous2007-516">[488]</a></sup> After strong protests by the German Catholic and Protestant churches in August 1941 Hitler ordered the cancellation of the T4 program,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELifton200090.E2.80.9395_517-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELifton200090.E2.80.9395-517">[489]</a></sup> although the disabled and mentally-ill continued to be killed until the end of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200048_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200048-31">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Homosexuals">Homosexuals</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Institut_f%C3%BCr_Sexualwissenschaft" title="Institut für Sexualwissenschaft">Institut für Sexualwissenschaft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pink_triangle" title="Pink triangle">Pink triangle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_homosexuals_in_Nazi_Germany_and_the_Holocaust" title="Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany and the Holocaust">Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany and the Holocaust</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reichszentrale-Erlass-1936.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Reichszentrale-Erlass-1936.jpg/170px-Reichszentrale-Erlass-1936.jpg" width="170" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Reichszentrale-Erlass-1936.jpg/255px-Reichszentrale-Erlass-1936.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Reichszentrale-Erlass-1936.jpg/340px-Reichszentrale-Erlass-1936.jpg 2x" data-file-width="647" data-file-height="922" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reichszentrale-Erlass-1936.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Himmler's</a> executive order from 1938 for the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Reich_Central_Office_for_the_Combating_of_Homosexuality_and_Abortion" title="Reich Central Office for the Combating of Homosexuality and Abortion">Reich's office against homosexuality.</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 5,000 and 15,000 German homosexuals are estimated to have been sent to concentration camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarran2000108_426-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarran2000108-426">[402]</a></sup> James Steakley writes that what mattered in Germany was criminal intent or character, rather than acts, and the <i>"gesundes Volksempfinden"</i> ("healthy sensibility of the people") became the guiding legal principle.<sup id="cite_ref-Steakley74_518-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steakley74-518">[490]</a></sup> In 1936, Himmler created the <a href="/wiki/Reich_Central_Office_for_the_Combating_of_Homosexuality_and_Abortion" title="Reich Central Office for the Combating of Homosexuality and Abortion">Reich Central Office for the Combating of Homosexuality and Abortion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2012237_519-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2012237-519">[491]</a></sup> Homosexuality was declared contrary to "wholesome popular sentiment".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarran2000108_426-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarran2000108-426">[402]</a></sup> The Gestapo raided <a href="/wiki/Gay_bar" title="Gay bar">gay bars</a>, tracked individuals using the address books of those they arrested, used the subscription lists of gay magazines to find others, and encouraged people to report suspected homosexual behavior and to scrutinize the behavior of their neighbors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarran2000108_426-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarran2000108-426">[402]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steakley74_518-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steakley74-518">[490]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tens of thousands were convicted between 1933 and 1944 and sent to camps for "rehabilitation", where they were identified by pink triangles.<sup id="cite_ref-Steakley74_518-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steakley74-518">[490]</a></sup> Hundreds were <a href="/wiki/Castration" title="Castration">castrated</a>, sometimes voluntarily in hopes that they could avoid criminal sentences, although in some cases the consent had been forced.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiles199245.E2.80.937_520-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiles199245.E2.80.937-520">[492]</a></sup> They were abused, tortured, used in medical experiments, and killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarran2000108_426-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarran2000108-426">[402]</a></sup> Steakley writes that the full extent of gay suffering was slow to emerge after the war. Many victims kept their stories to themselves because homosexuality remained criminalized in postwar Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Steakley74_518-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steakley74-518">[490]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_opponents">Political opponents</span></h4>
<p>German communists, socialists and trade unionists were among the earliest opponents of the Nazis,<sup id="cite_ref-521" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-521">[493]</a></sup> and they were also among the first to be sent to concentration camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015125_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015125-180">[171]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the invasion of the Soviet Union, Hitler issued the <a href="/wiki/Commissar_Order" title="Commissar Order">Commissar Order</a>, which ordered the execution of all political <a href="/wiki/Commissar" title="Commissar">commissars</a> and Communist Party members captured.<sup id="cite_ref-522" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-522">[494]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Nacht_und_Nebel" title="Nacht und Nebel">Nacht und Nebel</a></i> ("Night and Fog") was a directive of Hitler in December 1941, resulting in <a href="/wiki/Kidnapping" title="Kidnapping">kidnapping</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">disappearance</a> of political activists throughout the German occupied territories.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel2010184_523-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel2010184-523">[495]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="Jehovah's_Witnesses"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jehovah.27s_Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Persecution of Jehovah's Witnesses in Nazi Germany">Persecution of Jehovah's Witnesses in Nazi Germany</a></div>
<p>Because they refused to pledge allegiance to the Nazi party or to serve in the military, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> were sent to concentration camps where they were given the option of renouncing their faith and submitting to the state's authority.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilton2001346.E2.80.93349_524-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilton2001346.E2.80.93349-524">[496]</a></sup> They were marked out by purple triangles. The United States Holocaust Memorial Museum estimates between 2700 and 3300 were sent to concentration camps,<sup id="cite_ref-USHMMJW_427-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USHMMJW-427">[403]</a></sup> but Sybil Milton states the number in the camps was 10,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilton2001350_428-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilton2001350-428">[404]</a></sup> Between 1400<sup id="cite_ref-USHMMJW_427-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USHMMJW-427">[403]</a></sup> and 2500 died while in the camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilton2001350_428-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilton2001350-428">[404]</a></sup> Historian Detlef Garbe writes that "no other religious movement resisted the pressure to conform to National Socialism with comparable unanimity and steadfastness."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarbe2001251_525-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarbe2001251-525">[497]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniqueness_question">Uniqueness question</span></h2>
<p>Shimon Samuels says that one debate in Holocaust scholarship is between "specifists" and "universalists". The former regards comparisons of the Holocaust to other genocides to be invidious <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_trivialization" title="Holocaust trivialization">trivialization</a>, while the latter places the Holocaust alongside other experiences of mass killings as part and parcel of the global context of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> and human suffering.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESamuels2009259_526-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESamuels2009259-526">[498]</a></sup> Proponents of the Holocaust's uniqueness argue that comparing it to other genocides trivializes the Holocaust, with regards to its scope, scale, methods and motivations.<sup id="cite_ref-527" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-527">[499]</a></sup> Opponents of this view consider it immoral and unjustified to hold any tragedy as unique and beyond comparison. Others believe that debating the Holocaust's uniqueness itself is offensive and misguided.</p>
<p>A 2010 survey by Dan Stone deemed the debate "irrelevant" in genocide scholarship.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStone2011211.E2.80.93212_528-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStone2011211.E2.80.93212-528">[500]</a></sup> However specific arguments about the German Holocaust continue to characterize the views of many specialists on the subject. A 2015 view from a historian of the Third Reich, <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Evans" title="Richard J. Evans">Richard J. Evans</a>:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Thus although the Nazi 'Final Solution' was one genocide among many, it had features that made it stand out from all the rest as well. Unlike all the others it was bounded neither by space nor by time. It was launched not against a local or regional obstacle, but at a world-enemy seen as operating on a global scale. It was bound to an even larger plan of racial reordering and reconstruction involving further genocidal killing on an almost unimaginable scale, aimed, however, at clearing the way in a particular region – Eastern Europe – for a further struggle against the Jews and those the Nazis regarded as their puppets. It was set in motion by ideologues who saw world history in racial terms. It was, in part, carried out by industrial methods. These things all make it unique.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— Richard Evans, <i>The Third Reich in History and Memory</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2015385_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2015385-47">[42]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_the_Holocaust" title="Aftermath of the Holocaust">Aftermath of the Holocaust</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trials">Trials</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_trials" title="Nuremberg trials">Nuremberg trials</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dachau_trials" title="Dachau trials">Dachau trials</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Defendants_in_the_dock_at_the_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Defendants_in_the_dock_at_the_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg/220px-Defendants_in_the_dock_at_the_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Defendants_in_the_dock_at_the_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg/330px-Defendants_in_the_dock_at_the_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Defendants_in_the_dock_at_the_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg/440px-Defendants_in_the_dock_at_the_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2944" data-file-height="2274" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Defendants_in_the_dock_at_the_Nuremberg_Trials.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Defendants in the dock at the Nuremberg trials. The main target of the prosecution was <a href="/wiki/Hermann_G%C3%B6ring" title="Hermann Göring">Hermann Göring</a> (at the left edge on the first row of benches), considered to be the most important surviving official in the <i><a href="/wiki/Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a></i> after Hitler's death. Göring later committed suicide.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_trials" title="Nuremberg trials">Nuremberg trials</a> were a series of <a href="/wiki/Military_tribunal" class="mw-redirect" title="Military tribunal">military tribunals</a>, held by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied forces</a> after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>, Germany, to prosecute prominent members of the political, military, and economic leadership of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>. The first of these trials was the 1945–1946 trial of the major war criminals before the International Military Tribunal (IMT).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris2006106_529-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris2006106-529">[501]</a></sup> This tribunal tried 22 political and military leaders of the Third Reich,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder1976255_530-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder1976255-530">[502]</a></sup> except for <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels" title="Joseph Goebbels">Joseph Goebbels</a>, all of whom had committed suicide several months before.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiddiss2001643_531-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiddiss2001643-531">[503]</a></sup></p>
<p>The prosecution entered indictments against 24 major war criminals<sup id="cite_ref-532" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-532">[ac]</a></sup> and seven organizations—the leadership of the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> party, the Reich Cabinet, the <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">Schutzstaffel</a> (SS), <a href="/wiki/Sicherheitsdienst" title="Sicherheitsdienst">Sicherheitsdienst</a> (SD), the <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">Sturmabteilung</a> (SA) and the "General Staff and High Command". The indictments were for: participation in a <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(crime)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy (crime)">common plan or conspiracy</a> for the accomplishment of a <a href="/wiki/Crime_against_peace" title="Crime against peace">crime against peace</a>; planning, initiating and waging <a href="/wiki/War_of_aggression" title="War of aggression">wars of aggression</a> and other crimes against peace; <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Crime_against_humanity" class="mw-redirect" title="Crime against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>. The Tribunal passed out sentences ranging from acquittal to death by hanging.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiddiss2001643.E2.80.93644_533-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiddiss2001643.E2.80.93644-533">[504]</a></sup> Further trials at Nuremberg took place between 1946 and 1949, which tried a further 185 defendants.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiddiss2001646_534-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiddiss2001646-534">[505]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_languages">Effect on languages</span></h3>
<p>The Holocaust greatly affected Yiddish language and culture. On the eve of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, there were 11 to 13 million Yiddish speakers in the world. Five-sixths of the Jewish victims spoke Yiddish, which greatly reduced the number of speakers throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobs20053_535-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobs20053-535">[506]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reparations">Reparations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reparations_Agreement_between_Israel_and_West_Germany" title="Reparations Agreement between Israel and West Germany">Reparations Agreement between Israel and West Germany</a></div>
<p>In March 1951, a request was made by Israel which claimed global recompense to <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> of $1.5&#160;billion based on the financial cost absorbed by Israel for the rehabilitation of 500,000 Jewish survivors. <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West German</a> Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer" title="Konrad Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a> accepted these terms and declared he was ready to negotiate other reparations. A <a href="/wiki/Claims_Conference" title="Claims Conference">Conference on Jewish Material Claims against Germany</a> was opened in order to help with individual claims. After negotiations, the claim was reduced to a sum of $720&#160;million in direct and indirect compensation to be paid over a period of 12 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZweig2001531.E2.80.93532_536-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZweig2001531.E2.80.93532-536">[507]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1988, West Germany allocated another $125&#160;million for reparations. In 1999, many German industries such as <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> or <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a> faced lawsuits for their role in the <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II" title="Forced labour under German rule during World War II">forced labour during World War II</a>. In order to dismiss these lawsuits, Germany agreed to raise $5&#160;billion for reparations.<sup id="cite_ref-RestitutionJVL_537-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RestitutionJVL-537">[508]</a></sup> In 2013, Germany agreed to pay a new reparation of €772&#160;million as a result of negotiations with Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-538" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-538">[509]</a></sup> In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a>, the French state-owned railway company, was compelled to allocate $60&#160;million to American Jewish Holocaust survivors for its role in the transport of deportees to Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-539" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-539">[510]</a></sup> These reparations were sometimes criticized in Israel where they were seen as "blood money".<sup id="cite_ref-RestitutionJVL_537-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RestitutionJVL-537">[508]</a></sup></p>
