<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 60em; -webkit-column-width: 60em; column-width: 60em; list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The extended definition of the Holocaust includes other victims of Nazi crimes against humanity and war crimes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Romani genocide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Action_T4" class="mw-redirect" title="Action T4">Germany's eugenics program</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation" title="Nazi crimes against the Polish nation">Nazi crimes against the Polish nation</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> as well as political opponents, the <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_homosexuals_in_Nazi_Germany_and_the_Holocaust" title="Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany and the Holocaust">persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany and the Holocaust</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Persecution of Jehovah's Witnesses in Nazi Germany">persecution of Jehovah's Witnesses in Nazi Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200047.E2.80.9351_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200047.E2.80.9351-2">[2]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">From the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">ὁλόκαυστος</span> <i><span lang="el-Latn" xml:lang="el-Latn">holókaustos</span></i>: <i>hólos</i>, "whole" and <i>kaustós</i>, "burnt".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDawidowicz1986xxxvii_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDawidowicz1986xxxvii-4">[3]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>: <big><span lang="he" xml:lang="he">השואה</span></big>, <i>HaShoah</i>, "the catastrophe"</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Hebrew word <i>churban</i> is used by many <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Jews">Orthodox Jews</a> to refer to the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischel46_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischel46-13">[10]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Further examples include Ben Kiernan in <i>Blood and Soil</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKiernan2009454_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKiernan2009454-19">[15]</a></sup> Stephen Atkins in <i>Holocaust Denial as an International Movement</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAtkins200911_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAtkins200911-20">[16]</a></sup> Susan Zuccotti in <i>The Holocaust, the French, and the Jews</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZuccotti19935_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZuccotti19935-21">[17]</a></sup> Richard Evans in <i>Lying About Hitler</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2002104_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2002104-22">[18]</a></sup> Martin Gilbert in <i>The Holocaust</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert198518_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert198518-23">[19]</a></sup> and Adam Jones in <i>Genocide</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones2006147_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones2006147-24">[20]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-60">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It was originally formed after World War I as the German Workers' Party and changed its name in April 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder197663_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder197663-59">[54]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Nuremberg laws that reversed the empancipation of the Jews did not apply to Romanis as they had never emancipated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009p149_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009p149-89">[83]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-104">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The French planned to try Grynszpan for murder, but the German invasion in 1940 interrupted the proceedings. Grynszpan was handed over to the Germans and his fate is unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder1997301.E2.80.93302_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedl.C3.A4nder1997301.E2.80.93302-103">[96]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-158"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-158">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Only one would survive the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2016140_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2016140-157">[149]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-185"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-185">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Red signified a political prisoner,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015125_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015125-180">[171]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> had purple triangles,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015126_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015126-181">[172]</a></sup> "asocials" and criminals wore black or green, badges for homosexuals were pink,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015127_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015127-182">[173]</a></sup> and yellow for Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015623_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWachsmann2015623-183">[174]</a></sup> Jews had a second yellow triangle which was worn with their original triangle, with the two triangles forming a six-pointed star.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYahil1990134_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYahil1990134-184">[175]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-221"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-221">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The exact details of who killed whom and when are murky and have led to much debate in Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010196_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010196-220">[210]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-234"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-234">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Germans continued to use the ravine for mass killings throughout the war, and the total killed there could have been as high as 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016199_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016199-233">[222]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-251"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-251">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although not technically part of Operation <i>Reinhard</i>, <a href="/wiki/Che%C5%82mno_extermination_camp" title="Chełmno extermination camp">Chełmno</a> began functioning as an extermination camp in December 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-yvChelmno_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yvChelmno-250">[238]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-256"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-256">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Chełmno, which used gas vans rather than gas chambers to commit mass murder,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMontague201264.E2.80.9365_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontague201264.E2.80.9365-252">[239]</a></sup> had its roots in the extension of the Euthanasia Program <a href="/wiki/Action_T4" class="mw-redirect" title="Action T4">Action T4</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Warthegau" class="mw-redirect" title="Warthegau">Warthegau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMontague201214.E2.80.9316_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontague201214.E2.80.9316-253">[240]</a></sup> The camp was established in November 1941,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMontague201253.E2.80.9355_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontague201253.E2.80.9355-254">[241]</a></sup> but it did not begin the liquidation of large numbers of that <i><a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Nazi_Germany" title="Administrative divisions of Nazi Germany">Gau</a></i> Jews until December 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMontague201263_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontague201263-255">[242]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-258"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-258">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Majdanek began as a POW camp, but in August 1942 it had gas chambers installed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack201670.E2.80.9371_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack201670.E2.80.9371-257">[243]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-305"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-305">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The fighters probably only had, in the words of historian Doris Bergen, "a very few submachine guns, and some rifles" in addition to pistols, grenades, and homemade gasolene bombs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergen2016269_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergen2016269-304">[289]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-309"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-309">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">About 7000 died during the fighting and around 7000 sent to Treblinka.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECesarani2016616_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECesarani2016616-308">[292]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-314"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-314">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">About 100 prisoners were either recaptured before leaving the camp or did not even attempt to escape because of illness or other conditions. Another 350 to 400 inmates were killed before getting beyond the fence area. The rest of the prisoners managed to escape, but only about 200 survived the first 24 hours,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArad1987298_313-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArad1987298-313">[296]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-335"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-335">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The full extent of his work is unknown because <a href="/wiki/Otmar_von_Verschuer" class="mw-redirect" title="Otmar von Verschuer">Otmar von Verschuer</a> destroyed the correspondence Mengele sent to him while Mengele was at Auschwitz.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELifton2000358_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELifton2000358-334">[316]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-340"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-340">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The only exception was <a href="/wiki/Lodz_Ghetto" class="mw-redirect" title="Lodz Ghetto">Lodz Ghetto</a>, which was not liquidated until mid-1944.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003pp256-257_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkvan_Pelt2003pp256-257-339">[320]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-345"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-345">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One exception was the area around Bialystok, where over 100,000 Jews were deported to extermination camps – most going to Treblinka, but a few to Auschwitz.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2010352.E2.80.93353_344-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2010352.E2.80.93353-344">[324]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-365"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-365">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some reports have Karski also infiltrating Bełżec disguised as a guard,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELukas2012159_364-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELukas2012159-364">[343]</a></sup> but other sources state he snuck into a transit camp where Jews were sent on to Bełżec.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000183_363-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia2000183-363">[342]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-416"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-416">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There were over 42,000 camps and other facilities identified. Even in Berlin there were 3,000 camps of various functions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELichtblau2013_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELichtblau2013-173">[164]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-424"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-424">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The United States Holocaust Memorial Museum places the scholarly estimates at 220,000–500,000. According to Berenbaum "serious scholars estimate that between 90,000 and 220,000 were killed under German rule."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2005126_423-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerenbaum2005126-423">[400]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-456"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-456">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">6300 were Danish citizens and about 1500 were refugees.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-458"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-458">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The victims were 56,000 non-French Jews, 8000 naturalized Jewish citizens of France, 8000 non-citizen Jewish children, and 1500 Jews from Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009123_457-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009123-457">[432]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-459"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-459">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">About a third of the French victims were citizens, the rest were either immigrants after World War I or refugees.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-461"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-461">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It did deport some Jews from annexed regions, but these are included in the figures for the original country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802_454-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauerRozett19901799.E2.80.931802-454">[430]</a></sup> The total was 11,000 Jews deported from the various regions Bulgaria had annexed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009113_460-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBloxham2009113-460">[433]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-532"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-532">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Two of the indictments were dropped before the end of the trial. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Ley" title="Robert Ley">Robert Ley</a> committed suicide in prison, and <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Krupp" class="mw-redirect" title="Gustav Krupp">Gustav Krupp</a> was judged unfit for trial.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiddiss2001643_531-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiddiss2001643-531">[503]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<li><cite class="citation book">Hedgepeth, Sonja M.; Saidel, Rochelle G. (2010). <i>Sexual Violence against Jewish Women During the Holocaust</i>. Lebanon,&#160;NH: University Press of New England.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Holocaust&amp;rft.au=Saidel%2C+Rochelle+G.&amp;rft.aufirst=Sonja+M.&amp;rft.aulast=Hedgepeth&amp;rft.btitle=Sexual+Violence+against+Jewish+Women+During+the+Holocaust&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.place=Lebanon%2C+NH&amp;rft.pub=University+Press+of+New+England&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Ian_Kershaw" title="Ian Kershaw">Kershaw, Ian</a> (2008). <i>Hitler, the Germans, and the Final Solution</i>. New Haven, CT: Yale University Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-300-15127-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-300-15127-5">978-0-300-15127-5</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Holocaust&amp;rft.aufirst=Ian&amp;rft.aulast=Kershaw&amp;rft.btitle=Hitler%2C+the+Germans%2C+and+the+Final+Solution&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-300-15127-5&amp;rft.place=New+Haven%2C+CT&amp;rft.pub=Yale+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>

Stroud, UK: Tempus.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Holocaust&amp;rft.aufirst=Peter&amp;rft.aulast=Longerich&amp;rft.btitle=The+Unwritten+Order%3A+Hitler%27s+Role+in+the+Final+Solution&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.place=Stroud%2C+UK&amp;rft.pub=Tempus&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>

Bloomington,&#160;IN: <a href="/wiki/Indiana_University_Press" title="Indiana University Press">Indiana University Press</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Holocaust&amp;rft.aufirst=Robert+Jan&amp;rft.aulast=van+Pelt&amp;rft.btitle=The+Case+for+Auschwitz%3A+Evidence+from+the+Irving+Trial&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.place=Bloomington%2C+IN&amp;rft.pub=Indiana+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
